         <td>1 </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>The elections of 1992 marked the beginning of multiparty politics after more than 25 years of rule by KANU.<sup id="cite_ref-Keith_80-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keith-80">[80]</a></sup> Following skirmishes in the aftermath of the elections, 5,000 people were killed and a further 75,000 others displaced from their homes.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> In the next five years, many political alliances were formed in preparation for the next elections. In 1994, <a href="/wiki/Jaramogi_Oginga_Odinga" title="Jaramogi Oginga Odinga">Jaramogi Oginga Odinga</a> died and several coalitions joined his FORD Kenya party to form a new party called United National Democratic Alliance. However, this party was plagued with disagreements. In 1995, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Leakey" title="Richard Leakey">Richard Leakey</a> formed the Safina party, but it was denied registration until November 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCKenyaHist_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCKenyaHist-84">[84]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1996, KANU revised the constitution to allow Moi to remain president for another term. Subsequently, Moi stood for re-election and won a 5th term in 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> His win was strongly criticised by his major opponents, <a href="/wiki/Mwai_Kibaki" title="Mwai Kibaki">Kibaki</a> and <a href="/wiki/Raila_Odinga" title="Raila Odinga">Odinga</a>, as being fraudulent.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCKenyaHist_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCKenyaHist-84">[84]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-86">[86]</a></sup> Following this win, Moi was constitutionally barred from vying for another presidential term. Beginning in 1998, Moi attempted to influence the country's succession politics to have <a href="/wiki/Uhuru_Kenyatta" title="Uhuru Kenyatta">Uhuru Kenyatta</a> elected in the upcoming 2002 elections.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="President_Kibaki_and_the_road_to_a_new_constitution">President Kibaki and the road to a new constitution</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Mwai_Kibaki" title="Mwai Kibaki">Mwai Kibaki</a>, <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Mwai_Kibaki" title="Presidency of Mwai Kibaki">Presidency of Mwai Kibaki</a>, <a href="/wiki/2002_Kenyan_general_election" title="2002 Kenyan general election">2002 Kenyan general election</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2007_Kenyan_general_election" title="2007 Kenyan general election">2007 Kenyan general election</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Moi's plan to be replaced by Uhuru Kenyatta failed, and <a href="/wiki/Mwai_Kibaki" title="Mwai Kibaki">Mwai Kibaki</a>, running for the opposition coalition "National Rainbow Coalition" (<a href="/wiki/National_Rainbow_Coalition" title="National Rainbow Coalition">NARC</a>), was elected president. David Anderson (2003) reports the elections were judged free and fair by local and international observers, and seemed to mark a turning point in Kenya's democratic evolution.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-86">[86]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2005, Kenyans rejected a plan to replace the 1963 independence constitution with a new one.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> As a result, the elections of 2007 took place following the procedure set by the old constitution. Kibaki was re-elected in highly contested elections marred by <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_Kenyan_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="2007–08 Kenyan crisis">political and ethnic violence</a>. The main opposition leader, Raila Odinga, claimed that the election results were rigged and that he was the rightfully elected president. In the ensuing violence, 1,500 people were killed and another 600,000 were internally displaced, making it the worst <a href="/wiki/Civil_unrest" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil unrest">post-election violence</a> in Kenya. To stop the death and displacement of people, Kibaki and Odinga agreed to work together, with the latter taking the position of a prime minister.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> This made Odinga <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Kenya" title="Prime Minister of Kenya">the second prime minister of Kenya</a>. </p>
      <p>In July 2010, Kenya partnered with other East African countries to form the new East African Common Market within the <a href="/wiki/East_African_Community" title="East African Community">East African Community</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> In August 2010, Kenyans held a <a href="/wiki/2010_Kenyan_constitutional_referendum" title="2010 Kenyan constitutional referendum">referendum</a> and passed <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Kenya" title="Constitution of Kenya">a new constitution</a>, which limited presidential powers and devolved the central government.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCKenyaHist_84-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCKenyaHist-84">[84]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Devolution_of_government_and_separation_of_powers">Devolution of government and separation of powers</span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Kenya" class="mw-redirect" title="Administrative divisions of Kenya">Administrative divisions of Kenya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Kenya" title="Constitution of Kenya">Constitution of Kenya</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Uhuru_Kenyatta" title="Presidency of Uhuru Kenyatta">Presidency of Uhuru Kenyatta</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Following the passage of the new constitution, Kenya became a <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential</a> <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democratic</a> republic, whereby the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Kenya" title="President of Kenya">President of Kenya</a> is both <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>, and of a <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party system</a>. The new constitution also states that <a href="/wiki/Executive_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive power">executive powers</a> are exercised by the executive branch of government, headed by the president, who chairs the cabinet that is composed of people chosen from outside parliament. <a href="/wiki/Legislative_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative power">Legislative power</a> is vested exclusively in <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Kenya" title="Parliament of Kenya">Parliament</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judiciary</a> is independent of the executive and the legislature. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics_under_2010_constitution">Government and politics under 2010 constitution</span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="President_Kibaki_era">President Kibaki era</span></h4> 
      <p>Mwai Kibaki became the first president to serve under this new constitution while Uhuru Kenyatta became the first president elected under this constitution. </p>
      <p>In 2011, <a href="/wiki/Operation_Linda_Nchi" title="Operation Linda Nchi">Kenya began sending troops</a> to Somalia to fight the Islamic terror group <a href="/wiki/Al-Shabaab_(militant_group)" title="Al-Shabaab (militant group)">Al-Shabaab</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Kerry_Jokes_About_HIs_Height_Standing_With_Kenyan_President_Uhuru_Kenyatta_at_the_State_House_in_Nairobi_(28534132883).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Secretary_Kerry_Jokes_About_HIs_Height_Standing_With_Kenyan_President_Uhuru_Kenyatta_at_the_State_House_in_Nairobi_%2828534132883%29.jpg/220px-Secretary_Kerry_Jokes_About_HIs_Height_Standing_With_Kenyan_President_Uhuru_Kenyatta_at_the_State_House_in_Nairobi_%2828534132883%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Secretary_Kerry_Jokes_About_HIs_Height_Standing_With_Kenyan_President_Uhuru_Kenyatta_at_the_State_House_in_Nairobi_%2828534132883%29.jpg/330px-Secretary_Kerry_Jokes_About_HIs_Height_Standing_With_Kenyan_President_Uhuru_Kenyatta_at_the_State_House_in_Nairobi_%2828534132883%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Secretary_Kerry_Jokes_About_HIs_Height_Standing_With_Kenyan_President_Uhuru_Kenyatta_at_the_State_House_in_Nairobi_%2828534132883%29.jpg/440px-Secretary_Kerry_Jokes_About_HIs_Height_Standing_With_Kenyan_President_Uhuru_Kenyatta_at_the_State_House_in_Nairobi_%2828534132883%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4046" data-file-height="2697"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Kerry_Jokes_About_HIs_Height_Standing_With_Kenyan_President_Uhuru_Kenyatta_at_the_State_House_in_Nairobi_(28534132883).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Kenyan President <a href="/wiki/Uhuru_Kenyatta" title="Uhuru Kenyatta">Uhuru Kenyatta</a> with U.S. Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a>, 22 August 2016
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In mid-2011, two consecutive missed rainy seasons precipitated the worst <a href="/wiki/2011_East_Africa_drought" title="2011 East Africa drought">drought in East Africa</a> seen in 60 years. The northwestern <a href="/wiki/Turkana_District" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkana District">Turkana region</a> was especially affected,<sup id="cite_ref-RedCross_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RedCross-92">[92]</a></sup> with local schools shut down as a result.<sup id="cite_ref-Kscafthit_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kscafthit-93">[93]</a></sup> The crisis was reportedly over by early 2012 because of coordinated relief efforts. Aid agencies subsequently shifted their emphasis to recovery initiatives, including digging irrigation canals and distributing plant seeds.<sup id="cite_ref-Unsfisiobrr_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unsfisiobrr-94">[94]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The 3rd President of Kenya Mwai Kibaki ruled from 2002 until 2013. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="President_Kenyatta_first_term">President Kenyatta first term</span></h4> 
      <p>After Kibaki's tenure ended in 2013, Kenya held its <a href="/wiki/2013_Kenyan_general_election" title="2013 Kenyan general election">first general elections</a> after the new constitution had been passed. Uhuru Kenyatta won in a disputed election result, leading to a petition by the opposition leader, Raila Odinga. The supreme court upheld the election results and <a href="/wiki/Uhuru_Kenyatta" title="Uhuru Kenyatta">President Kenyatta</a> began his term with <a href="/wiki/William_Ruto" title="William Ruto">William Ruto</a> as the deputy president. Despite the outcome of this ruling, the Supreme Court and the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_Judge" class="mw-redirect" title="Supreme Court Judge">head of the Supreme Court</a> were seen as powerful institutions that could carry out their role of checking the powers of the president.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="President_Kenyatta_second_term">President Kenyatta second term</span></h4> 
      <p>In 2017, Uhuru Kenyatta won a second term in office in another <a href="/wiki/2017_Kenyan_general_election" title="2017 Kenyan general election">disputed election</a>. Following the defeat, Raila Odinga again petitioned the results in the Supreme Court, accusing the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Independent_Electoral_and_Bundaries_commission_of_Kenya&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Independent Electoral and Bundaries commission of Kenya (page does not exist)">electoral commission</a> of mismanagement of the elections and Uhuru Kenyatta and his party of rigging. The Supreme Court overturned the election results in what became a landmark ruling in Africa and one of the very few in the world in which the results of a presidential elections were annulled.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> This ruling solidified the position of the Supreme Court as an independent body.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Consequently, Kenya had a second round of elections for the presidential position, in which Uhuru emerged the winner after Raila refused to participate, citing irregularities.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="After_2018_Kenya_handshake">After 2018 Kenya handshake</span></h4> 
      <p>The historical <a href="/wiki/2018_Kenya_handshake" title="2018 Kenya handshake">handshake</a> in March 2018, between president Uhuru Kenyatta and his long-time opponent Raila Odinga, meant reconciliation followed by economic growth and increased stability.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="BBI_Initiative">BBI Initiative</span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Kenya#BBI_Initiative" title="Constitution of Kenya">Constitution of Kenya §&nbsp;BBI Initiative</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Between 2019 and 2021, President Kenyatta and Raila Odinga combined efforts to promote major changes to the Kenyan constitution, labeled as the "Building Bridges Initiative" (BBI), saying that their efforts were to improve inclusion and overcome the country's winner-take-all election system that often resulted in post-election violence.<sup id="cite_ref-bbi_blocked_2021_05_14_bbc_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbi_blocked_2021_05_14_bbc-102">[102]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kenyan_court_2021_05_13_reuters_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kenyan_court_2021_05_13_reuters-103">[103]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The BBI proposal called for broad expansion of the legislative and executive branches, including the creation of a <a href="/wiki/Prime_minister" title="Prime minister">prime minister</a> with two deputies and an official leader of the opposition, reverting to selecting cabinet ministers from among the elected Members of Parliament, establishment of up to 70 new <a href="/wiki/Constituencies" class="mw-redirect" title="Constituencies">constituencies</a>, and addition of up to 300 un-elected members of Parliament (under an "<a href="/wiki/Affirmative_action" title="Affirmative action">affirmative action</a>" plan).<sup id="cite_ref-bbi_blocked_2021_05_14_bbc_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbi_blocked_2021_05_14_bbc-102">[102]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kenyan_court_2021_05_13_reuters_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kenyan_court_2021_05_13_reuters-103">[103]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>However, critics saw it as unnecessary, and an attempt to reward political dynasties -- and blunt the efforts of Deputy President Willian Ruto (Odinga's rival for the next presidency) -- and bloating the government at an exceptional cost to the debt-laded country.<sup id="cite_ref-bbi_blocked_2021_05_14_bbc_102-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbi_blocked_2021_05_14_bbc-102">[102]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kenyan_court_2021_05_13_reuters_103-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kenyan_court_2021_05_13_reuters-103">[103]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Ultimately, in May 2021, the Kenyan High Court ruled that the BBI constitutional reform effort was unconstitutional, because it was not truly a <a href="/wiki/Popular_initiative" class="mw-redirect" title="Popular initiative">popular initiative</a>, but rather an effort of the government.<sup id="cite_ref-bbi_blocked_2021_05_14_bbc_102-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbi_blocked_2021_05_14_bbc-102">[102]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kenyan_court_2021_05_13_reuters_103-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kenyan_court_2021_05_13_reuters-103">[103]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The court sharply criticized Kenyatta for the attempt, laying out out grounds for his being sued, personally, or even <a href="/wiki/Impeachment" title="Impeachment">impeached</a> (though the Parliament, which had passed the BBI, was unlikely to do that). The ruling was seen as a major defeat for both Kenyatta (soon to leave office), and Odinga (expected to seek the presidency), but a boon to Odinga's future presidential-election rival, Ruto.<sup id="cite_ref-bbi_blocked_2021_05_14_bbc_102-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbi_blocked_2021_05_14_bbc-102">[102]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kenyan_court_2021_05_13_reuters_103-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kenyan_court_2021_05_13_reuters-103">[103]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Kenya" title="Geography of Kenya">Geography of Kenya</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Un-kenya.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Un-kenya.png/220px-Un-kenya.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="287" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Un-kenya.png/330px-Un-kenya.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Un-kenya.png/440px-Un-kenya.png 2x" data-file-width="2367" data-file-height="3092"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Un-kenya.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A map of Kenya.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_KEN_present.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Koppen-Geiger_Map_KEN_present.svg/220px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_KEN_present.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Koppen-Geiger_Map_KEN_present.svg/330px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_KEN_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Koppen-Geiger_Map_KEN_present.svg/440px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_KEN_present.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1290" data-file-height="850"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_KEN_present.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a> map of Kenya.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>At 580,367&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (224,081&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi),<sup id="cite_ref-cia_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-11">[11]</a></sup> Kenya is the world's forty-seventh largest country (after <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a>). It lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/5th_parallel_north" title="5th parallel north">5°N</a> and <a href="/wiki/5th_parallel_south" title="5th parallel south">5°S</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/34th_meridian_east" title="34th meridian east">34°</a> and <a href="/wiki/42nd_meridian_east" title="42nd meridian east">42°E</a>. From the coast on the Indian Ocean, the low plains rise to central highlands. The highlands are bisected by the <a href="/wiki/Kenyan_Rift_Valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Kenyan Rift Valley">Great Rift Valley</a>, with a fertile plateau lying to the east.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The Kenyan Highlands are one of the most successful agricultural production regions in Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-104">[104]</a></sup> The highlands are the site of the highest point in Kenya and the second highest peak on the continent: <a href="/wiki/Mount_Kenya" title="Mount Kenya">Mount Kenya</a>, which reaches a height of 5,199&nbsp;m (17,057&nbsp;ft) and is the site of glaciers. <a href="/wiki/Mount_Kilimanjaro" title="Mount Kilimanjaro">Mount Kilimanjaro</a> (5,895&nbsp;m or 19,341&nbsp;ft) can be seen from Kenya to the south of the Tanzanian border. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3> 
      <p>Kenya's climate varies from tropical along the coast to temperate inland to <a href="/wiki/Arid" title="Arid">arid</a> in the north and northeast parts of the country. The area receives a great deal of sunshine every month. It is usually cool at night and early in the morning inland at higher elevations. </p>
      <p>The "long rains" season occurs from March/April to May/June. The "short rains" season occurs from October to November/December. The rainfall is sometimes heavy and often falls in the afternoons and evenings. Climate change is altering the natural pattern of the rainfall period, causing an extension of the short rains, which has begat floods,<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> and reducing the drought cycle from every ten years to annual events, producing strong droughts such as the <a href="/wiki/2008-09_Kenya_Drought" class="mw-redirect" title="2008-09 Kenya Drought">2008-09 Kenya Drought</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The temperature remains high throughout these months of tropical rain. The hottest period is February and March, leading into the season of the long rains, and the coldest is in July, until mid-August.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-107">[107]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="excerpt-block">
       <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r952607947">.mw-parser-output .excerpt .selflink{font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .excerpt-indicator{border-left:3px solid #c8ccd1;margin:1em 0;padding-left:1em}</style>
       <div class="excerpt"> 
        <p><a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Kenya" title="Climate change in Kenya">Climate change in Kenya</a> is increasingly impacting the lives of Kenya's citizens and the environment.<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Kenya_ReliefWeb_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Kenya_ReliefWeb-108">[108]</a></sup> Climate change has led to more frequent <a href="/wiki/Extreme_weather" title="Extreme weather">extreme weather</a> events like droughts which last longer than usual, irregular and unpredictable rainfall, flooding and increasing temperatures. The effects of these climatic changes have made already existing challenges with <a href="/wiki/Water_security" title="Water security">water security</a>, <a href="/wiki/Food_security" title="Food security">food security</a> and economic growth even more difficult. Harvests and agricultural production which account for about 33%<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> of total <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">Gross Domestic Product (GDP)</a><sup id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Kenya_UNICEF_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Kenya_UNICEF-110">[110]</a></sup> are also at risk. The increased temperatures, <a href="/wiki/Rain" title="Rain">rainfall</a> variability in <a href="/wiki/Arid" title="Arid">arid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">semi-arid</a> areas, and strong <a href="/wiki/Wind" title="Wind">winds</a> associated with tropical <a href="/wiki/Cyclone" title="Cyclone">cyclones</a> have combined to create favorable conditions for the breeding and <a href="/wiki/Migration_(ecology)" title="Migration (ecology)">migration</a> of pests.<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Kenya_Salih_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Kenya_Salih-111">[111]</a></sup> An increase in temperature of up to 2.5°C by 2050 is predicted to increase the frequency of extreme events such as <a href="/wiki/Flood" title="Flood">floods</a> and <a href="/wiki/Drought" title="Drought">droughts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Kenya_ReliefWeb_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Kenya_ReliefWeb-108">[108]</a></sup> </p> Hot and dry conditions in <a href="/wiki/Arid" title="Arid">Arid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">Semi-Arid</a> Lands (ASALs) make <a href="/wiki/Drought" title="Drought">droughts</a> or <a href="/wiki/Flooding" class="mw-redirect" title="Flooding">flooding</a> brought on by extreme <a href="/wiki/Weather" title="Weather">weather</a> changes even more dangerous. Coastal communities are already experiencing <a href="/wiki/Sea_level_rise" title="Sea level rise">sea level rise</a> and associated challenges such as <a href="/wiki/Saltwater_intrusion" title="Saltwater intrusion">saltwater intrusion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Kenya_ReliefWeb_108-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Kenya_ReliefWeb-108">[108]</a></sup> All these factors impact at-risk populations like marginalized communities, women and the youth.<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Kenya_UNICEF_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Kenya_UNICEF-110">[110]</a></sup>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Kenya" title="Wildlife of Kenya">Wildlife of Kenya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Environmental_issues_in_Kenya" title="Environmental issues in Kenya">Environmental issues in Kenya</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Kenya has considerable land area devoted to <a href="/wiki/Wildlife" title="Wildlife">wildlife</a> habitats, including the <a href="/wiki/Masai_Mara" class="mw-redirect" title="Masai Mara">Masai Mara</a>, where <a href="/wiki/Blue_Wildebeest" class="mw-redirect" title="Blue Wildebeest">blue wildebeest</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Bovid" class="mw-redirect" title="Bovid">bovids</a> participate in a large-scale <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/migration" class="extiw" title="wikt:migration">annual migration</a>. More than 1 million wildebeest and 200,000 zebras participate in the migration across the <a href="/wiki/Mara_River" title="Mara River">Mara River</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Big_Five_Game" class="mw-redirect" title="Big Five Game">"Big Five"</a> game animals of Africa, that is the <a href="/wiki/Lion" title="Lion">lion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leopard" title="Leopard">leopard</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_buffalo" title="African buffalo">buffalo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhinoceros" title="Rhinoceros">rhinoceros</a>, and <a href="/wiki/African_elephant" title="African elephant">elephant</a>, can be found in Kenya and in the Masai Mara in particular. A significant population of other wild animals, reptiles, and birds can be found in the <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_parks_of_Kenya" title="List of national parks of Kenya">national parks</a> and game reserves in the country. The annual animal migration occurs between June and September, with millions of animals taking part, attracting valuable foreign tourism. Two million wildebeest migrate a distance of 2,900 kilometres (1,802&nbsp;mi) from the <a href="/wiki/Serengeti" title="Serengeti">Serengeti</a> in neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a> to the Masai Mara<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> in Kenya, in a constant clockwise fashion, searching for food and water supplies. This Serengeti Migration of the wildebeest is listed among the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Natural_Wonders_of_Africa" title="Seven Natural Wonders of Africa">Seven Natural Wonders of Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kenya had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 4.2/10, ranking it 133rd globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-115">[115]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Kenya" title="Politics of Kenya">Politics of Kenya</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mwai_Kibaki,_October_2003.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/cf/Mwai_Kibaki%2C_October_2003.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="175" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="150" data-file-height="175"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mwai_Kibaki,_October_2003.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Kenya's third president, <a href="/wiki/Mwai_Kibaki" title="Mwai Kibaki">Mwai Kibaki</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Kenya is a <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential</a> <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democratic</a> republic with a <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party system</a>. The president is both the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>. <a href="/wiki/Executive_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive power">Executive power</a> is exercised by the government. <a href="/wiki/Legislative_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative power">Legislative power</a> is vested in both the government and the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Kenya" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of Kenya">National Assembly</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Kenya" title="Senate of Kenya">Senate</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">Judiciary</a> is independent of the executive and the legislature. There has been growing concern, especially during former president Daniel arap Moi's tenure, that the executive was increasingly meddling with the affairs of the judiciary.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kenya has high levels of corruption according to <a href="/wiki/Transparency_International" title="Transparency International">Transparency International</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Corruption_Perceptions_Index" title="Corruption Perceptions Index">Corruption Perceptions Index</a> (CPI), a metric which attempts to gauge the prevalence of <a href="/wiki/Public_sector" title="Public sector">public-sector</a> corruption in various countries. In 2019, the nation placed 137th out of 180 countries in the index, with a score of 28 out of 100.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> However, there are several rather significant developments with regards to curbing corruption from the Kenyan government, for instance, the establishment of a new and independent <a href="/wiki/Ethics_and_Anti-Corruption_Commission" title="Ethics and Anti-Corruption Commission">Ethics and Anti-Corruption Commission (EACC)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:JUDICIARY.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/JUDICIARY.JPG/220px-JUDICIARY.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/JUDICIARY.JPG/330px-JUDICIARY.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/JUDICIARY.JPG/440px-JUDICIARY.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4896" data-file-height="3672"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:JUDICIARY.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Kenya" title="Supreme Court of Kenya">Supreme Court of Kenya</a> building.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Following general elections held in 1997, the Constitution of Kenya Review Act, designed to pave the way for more comprehensive amendments to the Kenyan constitution, was passed by the national parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In December 2002, Kenya held democratic and open elections, which were judged free and fair by most international observers.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> The 2002 elections marked an important turning point in Kenya's democratic evolution in that power was transferred peacefully from the <a href="/wiki/Kenya_African_National_Union" title="Kenya African National Union">Kenya African National Union</a> (KANU), which had ruled the country since independence, to the <a href="/wiki/National_Rainbow_Coalition" title="National Rainbow Coalition">National Rainbow Coalition</a> (NARC), a coalition of political parties. </p>
      <p>Under the presidency of <a href="/wiki/Mwai_Kibaki" title="Mwai Kibaki">Mwai Kibaki</a>, the new ruling coalition promised to focus its efforts on generating economic growth, combating corruption, improving education, and rewriting its constitution. A few of these promises have been met. There is free primary education.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> In 2007, the government issued a statement declaring that from 2008, secondary education would be heavily subsidised, with the government footing all tuition fees.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2013_elections_and_new_government">2013 elections and new government</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Kenyan_general_election,_2013" class="mw-redirect" title="Kenyan general election, 2013">Kenyan general election, 2013</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kenyan_local_elections,_2013" class="mw-redirect" title="Kenyan local elections, 2013">Kenyan local elections, 2013</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Under the new constitution and with President Kibaki prohibited by term limits from running for a third term, Deputy Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Uhuru_Kenyatta" title="Uhuru Kenyatta">Uhuru Kenyatta</a> ran for office. He won with 50.51% of the vote in March 2013. </p>
      <p>In December 2014, President <a href="/wiki/Uhuru_Kenyatta" title="Uhuru Kenyatta">Uhuru Kenyatta</a> signed a Security Laws Amendment Bill, which supporters of the law suggested was necessary to guard against armed groups. Opposition politicians, human rights groups, and nine Western countries criticised the security bill, arguing that it infringed on democratic freedoms. The governments of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> also collectively issued a press statement cautioning about the law's potential impact. Through the Jubilee Coalition, the Bill was later passed on 19 December in the National Assembly under acrimonious circumstances.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Kenya" title="Foreign relations of Kenya">Foreign relations of Kenya</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:President_Obama_visits_Nairobi_Kenya_July_2015_(20848405843).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/President_Obama_visits_Nairobi_Kenya_July_2015_%2820848405843%29.jpg/220px-President_Obama_visits_Nairobi_Kenya_July_2015_%2820848405843%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/President_Obama_visits_Nairobi_Kenya_July_2015_%2820848405843%29.jpg/330px-President_Obama_visits_Nairobi_Kenya_July_2015_%2820848405843%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/President_Obama_visits_Nairobi_Kenya_July_2015_%2820848405843%29.jpg/440px-President_Obama_visits_Nairobi_Kenya_July_2015_%2820848405843%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="980" data-file-height="653"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:President_Obama_visits_Nairobi_Kenya_July_2015_(20848405843).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> in Nairobi, July 2015
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Kenya has close ties with its fellow <a href="/wiki/Swahili_language" title="Swahili language">Swahili</a>-speaking neighbours in the <a href="/wiki/African_Great_Lakes" title="African Great Lakes">African Great Lakes</a> region. Relations with Uganda and Tanzania are generally strong, as the three nations work toward economic and social integration through common membership in the <a href="/wiki/East_African_Community" title="East African Community">East African Community</a>. </p>
      <p>Relations with Somalia have historically been tense, although there has been some military co-ordination against Islamist insurgents. Kenya has good relations with the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-upenn_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-upenn-124">[124]</a></sup> Kenya is one of the most pro-American nations in Africa, and the wider world.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>With <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court" title="International Criminal Court">International Criminal Court</a> trial dates scheduled in 2013 for both President Kenyatta and Deputy President <a href="/wiki/William_Ruto" title="William Ruto">William Ruto</a> related to the 2007 election aftermath, US president <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> chose not to visit the country during his <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_visits_to_Sub-Saharan_Africa#List_of_trips" title="United States presidential visits to Sub-Saharan Africa">mid-2013 African trip</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> Later in the summer, Kenyatta visited China at the invitation of President <a href="/wiki/Xi_Jinping" title="Xi Jinping">Xi Jinping</a> after a stop in Russia and not having visited the United States as president.<sup id="cite_ref-wp01_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wp01-127">[127]</a></sup> In July 2015, Obama visited Kenya, the first American president to visit the country while in office.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/British_Army_Training_Unit_Kenya" title="British Army Training Unit Kenya">British Army Training Unit Kenya</a> (BATUK) is used for the training of <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British</a> infantry battalions in the arid and rugged terrain of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Rift_Valley" title="Great Rift Valley">Great Rift Valley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Armed_forces">Armed forces</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Defence_Forces" title="Kenya Defence Forces">Kenya Defence Forces</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_060806-N-0411D-109_Kenyan_Army_Brig._Gen._and_Natural_Fire_Commanding_Officer,_Leonard_Ngondi,_left,_greets_U.S._Marine_Lt._Col._Steve_Nichols,_left,_at_Camp_Lonestar.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/US_Navy_060806-N-0411D-109_Kenyan_Army_Brig._Gen._and_Natural_Fire_Commanding_Officer%2C_Leonard_Ngondi%2C_left%2C_greets_U.S._Marine_Lt._Col._Steve_Nichols%2C_left%2C_at_Camp_Lonestar.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/US_Navy_060806-N-0411D-109_Kenyan_Army_Brig._Gen._and_Natural_Fire_Commanding_Officer%2C_Leonard_Ngondi%2C_left%2C_greets_U.S._Marine_Lt._Col._Steve_Nichols%2C_left%2C_at_Camp_Lonestar.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/US_Navy_060806-N-0411D-109_Kenyan_Army_Brig._Gen._and_Natural_Fire_Commanding_Officer%2C_Leonard_Ngondi%2C_left%2C_greets_U.S._Marine_Lt._Col._Steve_Nichols%2C_left%2C_at_Camp_Lonestar.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_060806-N-0411D-109_Kenyan_Army_Brig._Gen._and_Natural_Fire_Commanding_Officer,_Leonard_Ngondi,_left,_greets_U.S._Marine_Lt._Col._Steve_Nichols,_left,_at_Camp_Lonestar.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Kenyan Army Brig. Gen. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Leonard_Muriuki_Ngondi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Leonard Muriuki Ngondi (page does not exist)">Leonard Ngondi</a>, left,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (April 2017)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> greets U.S. Marine Lt. Col. Steve Nichols, left, at <a href="/w/index.php?title=Camp_Lonestar&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Camp Lonestar (page does not exist)">Camp Lonestar</a> in Kenya, 2006
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <b>Kenya Defence Forces</b> are the <a href="/wiki/Armed_forces" class="mw-redirect" title="Armed forces">armed forces</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Kenya" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Kenya">Republic of Kenya</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Army" title="Kenya Army">Kenya Army</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Navy" title="Kenya Navy">Kenya Navy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Air_Force" title="Kenya Air Force">Kenya Air Force</a> compose the National Defence Forces. The current Kenya Defence Forces were established, and its composition laid out, in Article 241 of the 2010 <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Kenya" title="Constitution of Kenya">Constitution of Kenya</a>; the KDF is governed by the Kenya Defence Forces Act of 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Kenya" title="President of Kenya">President of Kenya</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">commander-in-chief</a> of all the armed forces. </p>
      <p>The armed forces are regularly deployed in peacekeeping missions around the world. Further, in the aftermath of the national elections of December 2007 and the violence that subsequently engulfed the country, a commission of inquiry, the <a href="/wiki/Waki_Commission" title="Waki Commission">Waki Commission</a>, commended its readiness and adjudged it to "have performed its duty well."<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> Nevertheless, there have been serious allegations of human rights violations, most recently while conducting counter-insurgency operations in the <a href="/wiki/Mt_Elgon" class="mw-redirect" title="Mt Elgon">Mt Elgon</a> area<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> and also in the district of <a href="/wiki/Mandera" title="Mandera">Mandera</a> central.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kenya's armed forces, like many government institutions in the country, have been tainted by <a href="/wiki/Corruption_in_Kenya" title="Corruption in Kenya">corruption</a> allegations. Because the operations of the armed forces have been traditionally cloaked by the ubiquitous blanket of "state security", the corruption has been hidden from public view, and thus less subject to public scrutiny and notoriety. This has changed recently. In what are by Kenyan standards unprecedented revelations, in 2010, credible claims of corruption were made with regard to recruitment<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> and procurement of armoured personnel carriers.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> Further, the wisdom and prudence of certain decisions of procurement have been publicly questioned.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_Kenya" title="Counties of Kenya">Counties of Kenya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Divisions_of_Kenya" title="Divisions of Kenya">Divisions of Kenya</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Map_showing_Counties_underthe_new_kenyan_constitution..gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Map_showing_Counties_underthe_new_kenyan_constitution..gif/220px-Map_showing_Counties_underthe_new_kenyan_constitution..gif" decoding="async" width="220" height="285" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Map_showing_Counties_underthe_new_kenyan_constitution..gif/330px-Map_showing_Counties_underthe_new_kenyan_constitution..gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Map_showing_Counties_underthe_new_kenyan_constitution..gif/440px-Map_showing_Counties_underthe_new_kenyan_constitution..gif 2x" data-file-width="620" data-file-height="804"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Map_showing_Counties_underthe_new_kenyan_constitution..gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Kenya's <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_Kenya" title="Counties of Kenya">47 counties</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Kenya is divided into <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_Kenya" title="Counties of Kenya">47 semi-autonomous counties</a> that are headed by governors. These 47 counties form the first-order divisions of Kenya. </p>
      <p>The smallest administrative units in Kenya are called <a href="/wiki/Locations_of_Kenya" title="Locations of Kenya">locations</a>. Locations often coincide with electoral wards. Locations are usually named after their central villages/towns. Many larger towns consist of several locations. Each location has a chief, appointed by the state. </p>
      <p>Constituencies are an electoral subdivision, with each county comprising a whole number of constituencies. An interim boundaries commission was formed in 2010 to review the constituencies and in its report, it recommended the creation of an additional 80 constituencies. Previous to the 2013 elections, there were 210 <a href="/wiki/Constituencies_of_Kenya" class="mw-redirect" title="Constituencies of Kenya">constituencies in Kenya</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Kenya" title="Human rights in Kenya">Human rights in Kenya</a>, <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Kenya" title="LGBT rights in Kenya">LGBT rights in Kenya</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Human_trafficking_in_Kenya" title="Human trafficking in Kenya">Human trafficking in Kenya</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">Homosexual acts</a> are illegal in Kenya and punishable by up to 14 years in prison, though the state often turns a blind eye to prosecuting gay people.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> According to a 2013 survey by the <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a>, 90% of Kenyans believe that homosexuality should not be accepted by society.<sup id="cite_ref-pewglobal.org_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pewglobal.org-141">[141]</a></sup> While addressing a joint press conference together with President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> in 2015, President Kenyatta declined to assure Kenya's commitment to gay rights, saying that "the issue of gay rights is really a non-issue... But there are some things that we must admit we don't share. Our culture, our societies don't accept."<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In November 2008, <a href="/wiki/WikiLeaks" title="WikiLeaks">WikiLeaks</a> brought wide international attention<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> to <i>The Cry of Blood</i> report, which documents the extrajudicial killing of gangsters by the Kenyan police. In the report, the <a href="/wiki/Kenya_National_Commission_on_Human_Rights" title="Kenya National Commission on Human Rights">Kenya National Commission on Human Rights</a> (KNCHR) reported these in their key finding "e)", stating that the <a href="/wiki/Forced_disappearance" title="Forced disappearance">forced disappearances</a> and <a href="/wiki/Extrajudicial_killing" title="Extrajudicial killing">extrajudicial killings</a> appeared to be official policy sanctioned by the political leadership and the police.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Kenya" title="Economy of Kenya">Economy of Kenya</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kenya_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Kenya_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg/350px-Kenya_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg.png" decoding="async" width="350" height="350" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Kenya_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg/525px-Kenya_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Kenya_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg/700px-Kenya_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="900"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kenya_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A proportional representation of Kenya's exports.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Kenya's <a href="/wiki/Macroeconomics" title="Macroeconomics">macroeconomic</a> outlook has steadily posted robust growth over the past few decades, mostly from road and rail infrastructure projects. However, much of this growth has come from cash flows diverted from ordinary Kenyan pockets at the <a href="/wiki/Microeconomics" title="Microeconomics">microeconomic</a> level through targeted <a href="/wiki/Monetary_policy" title="Monetary policy">monetary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fiscal_policy" title="Fiscal policy">fiscal</a> measures coupled with poor management, <a href="/wiki/Corruption" title="Corruption">corruption</a>, massive theft of public funds, <a href="/wiki/Freedom_and_the_law" class="mw-redirect" title="Freedom and the law">overlegislation</a>, and an ineffective <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judiciary</a>, resulting in diminished incomes in ordinary households and <a href="/wiki/Small_business" title="Small business">small businesses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Unemployment" title="Unemployment">unemployment</a>, <a href="/wiki/Underemployment" title="Underemployment">underemployment</a>, and general discontent across multiple sectors. Kenya ranks poorly on the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Fragile_States_Index" title="List of countries by Fragile States Index">Fragile States Index</a> at number 25 out of 178 countries, ranked in 2019, and is placed in the ALERT category. In 2014, the country's macroeconomic indicators were re-based, causing the <a href="/wiki/GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP">GDP</a> to shift upwards to low-middle-income country status. </p>
      <p>Kenya has a <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> (HDI) of 0.555 (medium), ranked 145 out of 186 in the world. As of 2005<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kenya&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 17.7% of Kenyans lived on less than $1.25 a day. <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELudeki_ChweyaJohn_Kithome_TutaS._Kichamu_Akivaga2005_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELudeki_ChweyaJohn_Kithome_TutaS._Kichamu_Akivaga2005-146">[146]</a></sup> In 2017, Kenya ranked 92nd in the World Bank <a href="/wiki/Ease_of_doing_business_index" title="Ease of doing business index">ease of doing business</a> rating from 113rd in 2016 (of 190 countries).<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> The important agricultural sector is one of the least developed and largely inefficient, employing 75% of the workforce compared to less than 3% in the <a href="/wiki/Food_security" title="Food security">food secure</a> <a href="/wiki/Developed_countries" class="mw-redirect" title="Developed countries">developed countries</a>. Kenya is usually classified as a <a href="/wiki/Frontier_market" class="mw-redirect" title="Frontier market">frontier market</a> or occasionally an <a href="/wiki/Emerging_market" title="Emerging market">emerging market</a>, but it is not one of the <a href="/wiki/Least_developed_countries" title="Least developed countries">least developed countries</a>. </p>
      <p>The economy has seen much expansion, seen by strong performance in tourism, higher education, and <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Kenya" title="Telecommunications in Kenya">telecommunications</a>, and decent post-drought results in agriculture, especially the vital tea sector.<sup id="cite_ref-lcweb2.loc.gov_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lcweb2.loc.gov-148">[148]</a></sup> Kenya's economy grew by more than 7% in 2007, and its foreign debt was greatly reduced.<sup id="cite_ref-lcweb2.loc.gov_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lcweb2.loc.gov-148">[148]</a></sup> This changed immediately after the disputed presidential election of December 2007, following the chaos which engulfed the country. </p>
      <p>Telecommunications and financial activity over the last decade now comprise 62% of GDP. 22% of GDP still comes from the unreliable agricultural sector which employs 75% of the labour force (a consistent characteristic of under-developed economies that have not attained <a href="/wiki/Food_security" title="Food security">food security</a>—an important catalyst of economic growth). A small portion of the population relies on food aid.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-149">[149]</a></sup> Industry and manufacturing is the smallest sector, accounting for 16% of GDP. The service, industry and manufacturing sectors only employ 25% of the labour force but contribute 75% of GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-lcweb2.loc.gov_148-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lcweb2.loc.gov-148">[148]</a></sup> Kenya also exports textiles worth over $400 million under <a href="/wiki/AGOA" class="mw-redirect" title="AGOA">AGOA</a>. </p>
      <p>Privatisation of state corporations like the defunct Kenya Post and Telecommunications Company, which resulted in East Africa's most profitable company—<a href="/wiki/Safaricom" title="Safaricom">Safaricom</a>, has led to their revival because of massive private investment. </p>
      <p>As of May&nbsp;2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kenya&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, economic prospects are positive with 4–5% GDP growth expected, largely because of expansions in <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications" class="mw-redirect" title="Telecommunications">telecommunications</a>, transport, construction, and a recovery in <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a>. The <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> estimated growth of 4.3% in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-WorldBanki_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WorldBanki-150">[150]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kenya,_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Kenya%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png/350px-Kenya%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png" decoding="async" width="350" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4c/Kenya%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png 1.5x" data-file-width="441" data-file-height="188"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kenya,_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Kenya, Trends in the Human Development Index 1970–2010.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In March 1996, the presidents of Kenya, Tanzania, and Uganda re-established the <a href="/wiki/East_African_Community" title="East African Community">East African Community</a> (EAC). The EAC's objectives include harmonising tariffs and customs regimes, free movement of people, and improving regional infrastructures. In March 2004, the three East African countries signed a <a href="/wiki/Customs_union" title="Customs union">Customs Union Agreement</a>. </p>
      <p>Kenya has a more developed financial services sector than its neighbours. The <a href="/wiki/Nairobi_Securities_Exchange" title="Nairobi Securities Exchange">Nairobi Securities Exchange</a> (NSE) is ranked 4th in Africa in terms of market capitalisation. The Kenyan banking system is supervised by the <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_Kenya" title="Central Bank of Kenya">Central Bank of Kenya</a> (CBK). As of late July 2004, the system consisted of 43 commercial banks (down from 48 in 2001) and several <a href="/wiki/Non-bank_financial_institution" title="Non-bank financial institution">non-bank financial institutions</a> including mortgage companies, four savings and loan associations, and several core foreign-exchange bureaus.<sup id="cite_ref-lcweb2.loc.gov_148-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lcweb2.loc.gov-148">[148]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Kenya" title="Tourism in Kenya">Tourism in Kenya</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Elephants_at_Amboseli_national_park_against_Mount_Kilimanjaro.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Elephants_at_Amboseli_national_park_against_Mount_Kilimanjaro.jpg/220px-Elephants_at_Amboseli_national_park_against_Mount_Kilimanjaro.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Elephants_at_Amboseli_national_park_against_Mount_Kilimanjaro.jpg/330px-Elephants_at_Amboseli_national_park_against_Mount_Kilimanjaro.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Elephants_at_Amboseli_national_park_against_Mount_Kilimanjaro.jpg/440px-Elephants_at_Amboseli_national_park_against_Mount_Kilimanjaro.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="533"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">

         </div><a href="/wiki/Amboseli_National_Park" title="Amboseli National Park">Amboseli National Park</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tsavo_east_panorama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Tsavo_east_panorama.jpg/220px-Tsavo_east_panorama.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="77" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Tsavo_east_panorama.jpg/330px-Tsavo_east_panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Tsavo_east_panorama.jpg/440px-Tsavo_east_panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6986" data-file-height="2433"></a>
