        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Kenya" title="Tourism in Kenya">Tourism in Kenya</a> is the second-largest source of foreign exchange revenue following agriculture.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> The Kenya Tourism Board is responsible for maintaining information pertaining to tourism in Kenya.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> The main tourist attractions are photo safaris through the <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_parks_of_Kenya" title="List of national parks of Kenya">60 national parks</a> and game reserves. Other attractions include the <a href="/wiki/Wildebeest" title="Wildebeest">wildebeest</a> migration at the <a href="/wiki/Masaai_Mara" class="mw-redirect" title="Masaai Mara">Masaai Mara</a>, which is considered to be the 7th wonder of the world; historical mosques, and colonial-era forts at <a href="/wiki/Mombasa" title="Mombasa">Mombasa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malindi" title="Malindi">Malindi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lamu" title="Lamu">Lamu</a>; renowned scenery such as the white-capped <a href="/wiki/Mount_Kenya" title="Mount Kenya">Mount Kenya</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Great_Rift_Valley,_Kenya" title="Great Rift Valley, Kenya">Great Rift Valley</a>; tea plantations at <a href="/wiki/Kericho" title="Kericho">Kericho</a>; coffee plantations at <a href="/wiki/Thika" title="Thika">Thika</a>; a splendid view of <a href="/wiki/Mount_Kilimanjaro" title="Mount Kilimanjaro">Mount Kilimanjaro</a> across the border into <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-ne_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ne-154">[154]</a></sup> and the beaches along the <a href="/wiki/Swahili_Coast" class="mw-redirect" title="Swahili Coast">Swahili Coast</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a>. Tourists, the largest number being from <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, are attracted mainly to the coastal beaches and the <a href="/wiki/Game_reserve" title="Game reserve">game reserves</a>, notably, the expansive <a href="/wiki/Tsavo_East_National_Park" title="Tsavo East National Park">East</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tsavo_West_National_Park" title="Tsavo West National Park">Tsavo West National Park</a>, 20,808 square kilometres (8,034&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) to the southeast. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Kenya" title="Agriculture in Kenya">Agriculture in Kenya</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kenya-Tealand-Near-Kericho-2012.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Kenya-Tealand-Near-Kericho-2012.JPG/220px-Kenya-Tealand-Near-Kericho-2012.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Kenya-Tealand-Near-Kericho-2012.JPG/330px-Kenya-Tealand-Near-Kericho-2012.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Kenya-Tealand-Near-Kericho-2012.JPG/440px-Kenya-Tealand-Near-Kericho-2012.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="2794"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kenya-Tealand-Near-Kericho-2012.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Tea farm near <a href="/wiki/Kericho" title="Kericho">Kericho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kericho_County" title="Kericho County">Kericho County</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Agriculture is the second largest contributor to Kenya's gross domestic product (GDP) after the service sector. In 2005, agriculture, including <a href="/wiki/Forestry" title="Forestry">forestry</a> and fishing, accounted for 24% of GDP, as well as for 18% of wage employment and 50% of revenue from exports. The principal <a href="/wiki/Cash_crop" title="Cash crop">cash crops</a> are tea, horticultural produce, and coffee. Horticultural produce and tea are the main growth sectors and the two most valuable of all of Kenya's exports. The production of major food staples such as <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">corn</a> is subject to sharp weather-related fluctuations. Production downturns periodically necessitate food aid—for example in 2004, due to one of Kenya's intermittent <a href="/wiki/Droughts" class="mw-redirect" title="Droughts">droughts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A consortium led by the <a href="/wiki/International_Crops_Research_Institute_for_the_Semi-Arid_Tropics" title="International Crops Research Institute for the Semi-Arid Tropics">International Crops Research Institute for the Semi-Arid Tropics</a> (<a href="/wiki/ICRISAT" class="mw-redirect" title="ICRISAT">ICRISAT</a>) has had some success in helping farmers grow new <a href="/wiki/Pigeon_pea" title="Pigeon pea">pigeon pea</a> varieties instead of maize, in particularly dry areas. Pigeon peas are very drought-resistant, so can be grown in areas with less than 650&nbsp;mm annual rainfall. Successive projects encouraged the commercialisation of legumes by stimulating the growth of local seed production and agro-dealer networks for distribution and marketing. This work, which included linking producers to wholesalers, helped to increase local producer prices by 20–25% in Nairobi and Mombasa. The commercialisation of the pigeon pea is now enabling some farmers to buy assets ranging from mobile phones to productive land and livestock, and is opening pathways for them to move out of poverty.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Tea, coffee, sisal, pyrethrum, corn, and wheat are grown in the fertile highlands, one of the most successful agricultural production regions in Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-104">[104]</a></sup> Livestock predominates in the semi-arid savanna to the north and east. <a href="/wiki/Coconuts" class="mw-redirect" title="Coconuts">Coconuts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pineapples" class="mw-redirect" title="Pineapples">pineapples</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cashew_nuts" class="mw-redirect" title="Cashew nuts">cashew nuts</a>, cotton, <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sisal" title="Sisal">sisal</a>, and corn are grown in the lower-lying areas. Kenya has not attained the level of investment and efficiency in agriculture that can guarantee food security, and coupled with resulting poverty (53% of the population lives below the poverty line), a significant portion of the population regularly starves and is heavily dependent on food aid.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_149-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-149">[149]</a></sup> Poor roads, an inadequate railway network, under-used water transport, and expensive air transport have isolated mostly <a href="/wiki/Arid" title="Arid">arid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid" class="mw-redirect" title="Semi-arid">semi-arid</a> areas, and farmers in other regions often leave food to rot in the fields because they cannot access markets. This was last seen in August and September 2011, prompting the <a href="/wiki/Kenyans_for_Kenya" title="Kenyans for Kenya">Kenyans for Kenya</a> initiative by the <a href="/wiki/Red_Cross" class="mw-redirect" title="Red Cross">Red Cross</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kapsowar1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Kapsowar1.JPG/220px-Kapsowar1.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Kapsowar1.JPG/330px-Kapsowar1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Kapsowar1.JPG/440px-Kapsowar1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kapsowar1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Agricultural countryside in Kenya
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Kenya's <a href="/wiki/Irrigation" title="Irrigation">irrigation</a> sector is categorised into three organizational types: <a href="/wiki/Smallholding" title="Smallholding">smallholder</a> schemes, centrally-managed public schemes, and private/commercial irrigation schemes. </p>
      <p>The smallholder schemes are owned, developed, and managed by individuals or groups of farmers operating as water users or self-help groups. Irrigation is carried out on individual or on group farms averaging 0.1–0.4 ha. There are about 3,000 smallholder irrigation schemes covering a total area of 47,000 ha. The country has seven large, centrally managed irrigation schemes, namely Mwea, <a href="/wiki/Bura_irrigation_and_Settlement_Project_(Kenya)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bura irrigation and Settlement Project (Kenya)">Bura</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hola,_Kenya" title="Hola, Kenya">Hola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Perkerra_River" title="Perkerra River">Perkera</a>, West Kano, Bunyala, and <a href="/wiki/Ahero" title="Ahero">Ahero</a>, covering a total area of 18,200 ha and averaging 2,600 ha per scheme. These schemes are managed by the National Irrigation Board and account for 18% of irrigated land area in Kenya. Large-scale private commercial farms cover 45,000 hectares, accounting for 40% of irrigated land. They utilise high technology and produce high-value crops for the export market, especially flowers and vegetables.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kenya is the world's 3rd largest exporter of <a href="/wiki/Cut_flowers" title="Cut flowers">cut flowers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-kenya-flower-industry_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kenya-flower-industry-159">[159]</a></sup> Roughly half of Kenya's 127 flower farms are concentrated around <a href="/wiki/Lake_Naivasha" title="Lake Naivasha">Lake Naivasha</a>, 90 kilometres northwest of Nairobi.<sup id="cite_ref-kenya-flower-industry_159-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kenya-flower-industry-159">[159]</a></sup> To speed their export, Nairobi airport has a terminal dedicated to the transport of flowers and vegetables.<sup id="cite_ref-kenya-flower-industry_159-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kenya-flower-industry-159">[159]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry_and_manufacturing">Industry and manufacturing</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Orrling_of_Nairobi.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Orrling_of_Nairobi.jpg/300px-Orrling_of_Nairobi.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="111" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Orrling_of_Nairobi.jpg/450px-Orrling_of_Nairobi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Orrling_of_Nairobi.jpg/600px-Orrling_of_Nairobi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6152" data-file-height="2269"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Orrling_of_Nairobi.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Commercial_Bank" class="mw-redirect" title="Kenya Commercial Bank">Kenya Commercial Bank</a> office at KENCOM House (right) in Nairobi.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Although Kenya is a low middle-income country, manufacturing accounts for 14% of the GDP, with industrial activity concentrated around the three largest urban centres of <a href="/wiki/Nairobi" title="Nairobi">Nairobi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mombasa" title="Mombasa">Mombasa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kisumu" title="Kisumu">Kisumu</a>, and is dominated by food-processing industries such as grain milling, beer production, sugarcane crushing, and the fabrication of consumer goods, e.g., vehicles from kits. </p>
      <p>Kenya also has a cement production industry.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> Kenya has an <a href="/wiki/Oil_refinery" title="Oil refinery">oil refinery</a> that processes imported crude petroleum into petroleum products, mainly for the domestic market. In addition, a substantial and expanding <a href="/wiki/Informal_sector" class="mw-redirect" title="Informal sector">informal sector</a> commonly referred to as <i>jua kali</i> engages in small-scale manufacturing of household goods, auto parts, and farm implements.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kenya's inclusion among the beneficiaries of the US Government's African Growth and Opportunity Act (<a href="/wiki/AGOA" class="mw-redirect" title="AGOA">AGOA</a>) has given a boost to manufacturing in recent years. Since AGOA took effect in 2000, Kenya's clothing sales to the United States increased from US$44&nbsp;million to US$270&nbsp;million (2006).<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> Other initiatives to strengthen manufacturing have been the new government's favourable tax measures, including the removal of duty on capital equipment and other raw materials.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Kenya" title="Transport in Kenya">Transport in Kenya</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The country has an extensive network of paved and unpaved roads. Kenya's railway system links the nation's ports and major cities, connecting it with neighbouring Uganda. There are 15 airports which have paved runways. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Kenya" title="Energy in Kenya">Energy in Kenya</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Worker_in_Olkaria_Kenya.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Worker_in_Olkaria_Kenya.jpg/170px-Worker_in_Olkaria_Kenya.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Worker_in_Olkaria_Kenya.jpg/255px-Worker_in_Olkaria_Kenya.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Worker_in_Olkaria_Kenya.jpg/340px-Worker_in_Olkaria_Kenya.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="800"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Worker_in_Olkaria_Kenya.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Workers at <a href="/wiki/Olkaria_II_Geothermal_Power_Station" title="Olkaria II Geothermal Power Station">Olkaria Geothermal Power Plant</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The largest share of Kenya's electricity supply comes from geothermal energy,<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> followed by hydroelectric stations at dams along the upper <a href="/wiki/Tana_River_(Kenya)" title="Tana River (Kenya)">Tana River</a>, as well as the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkwel_Gorge_Dam&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Turkwel Gorge Dam (page does not exist)">Turkwel Gorge Dam</a> in the west. A petroleum-fired plant on the coast, <a href="/wiki/Geothermal_power_in_Kenya" title="Geothermal power in Kenya">geothermal facilities</a> at <a href="/wiki/Olkaria" title="Olkaria">Olkaria</a> (near Nairobi), and electricity imported from <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a> make up the rest of the supply. A <a href="/wiki/Sodo%E2%80%93Moyale%E2%80%93Suswa_High_Voltage_Power_Line" title="Sodo–Moyale–Suswa High Voltage Power Line">2,000 MW powerline from Ethiopia</a> is nearing completion. </p>
      <p>Kenya's installed capacity increased from 1,142 <a href="/wiki/Megawatts" class="mw-redirect" title="Megawatts">megawatts</a> between 2001 and 2003 to 2,341 in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> The state-owned <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Electricity_Generating_Company" title="Kenya Electricity Generating Company">Kenya Electricity Generating Company (KenGen)</a>, established in 1997 under the name of Kenya Power Company, handles the generation of electricity, while Kenya Power handles the electricity transmission and distribution system in the country. Shortfalls of electricity occur periodically, when drought reduces water flow. To become energy sufficient, Kenya has installed <a href="/wiki/Wind_power_in_Kenya" title="Wind power in Kenya">wind power</a> and <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_in_Kenya" class="mw-redirect" title="Solar power in Kenya">solar power</a> (over 300 MW each), and aims to build a nuclear power plant by 2027.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kenya has proven deposits of oil in <a href="/wiki/Turkana_County" title="Turkana County">Turkana</a>. <a href="/wiki/Tullow_Oil" title="Tullow Oil">Tullow Oil</a> estimates the country's oil reserves to be around one billion barrels.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> Exploration is still continuing to determine if there are more reserves. Kenya currently imports all crude petroleum requirements. The country has no strategic reserves and relies solely on oil marketers' 21-day oil reserves required under industry regulations. Petroleum accounts for 20% to 25% of the national import bill.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chinese_investment_and_trade">Chinese investment and trade</span></h3> 
      <p>Published comments on Kenya's <a href="/wiki/98.4_Capital_FM" title="98.4 Capital FM">Capital FM</a> website by Liu Guangyuan, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Ambassador_to_Kenya" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese Ambassador to Kenya">China's ambassador to Kenya</a>, at the time of President Kenyatta's 2013 trip to Beijing, said, "Chinese investment in Kenya&nbsp;... reached $474 million, representing Kenya's largest source of foreign direct investment, and&nbsp;... bilateral trade&nbsp;... reached $2.84 billion" in 2012. Kenyatta was "[a]ccompanied by 60 Kenyan business people [and hoped to]&nbsp;... gain support from China for a planned $2.5 billion railway from the southern Kenyan port of Mombasa to neighboring <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a>, as well as a nearly $1.8 billion dam", according to a statement from the president's office, also at the time of the trip.<sup id="cite_ref-wp01_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wp01-127">[127]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Base Titanium, a subsidiary of Base resources of Australia, shipped its first major consignment of minerals to China. About 25,000 tonnes of <a href="/wiki/Ilmenite" title="Ilmenite">ilmenite</a> was flagged off the Kenyan coastal town of Kilifi. The first shipment was expected to earn Kenya about KSh15–20 billion in earnings.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> In 2014, the Chinese contracted railway project from Nairobi to Mombasa was suspended due to a dispute over compensation for land acquisition.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vision_2030">Vision 2030</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vision2030_logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Vision2030_logo.svg/220px-Vision2030_logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="96" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Vision2030_logo.svg/330px-Vision2030_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Vision2030_logo.svg/440px-Vision2030_logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1525" data-file-height="663"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vision2030_logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The official logo of <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Vision_2030" title="Kenya Vision 2030">Vision 2030</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2007, the Kenyan government unveiled <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Vision_2030" title="Kenya Vision 2030">Vision 2030</a>, an economic development programme it hopes will put the country in the same league as the <a href="/wiki/Four_Asian_Tigers" title="Four Asian Tigers">Asian Economic Tigers</a> by the year 2030. In 2013, it launched a National Climate Change Action Plan, having acknowledged that omitting climate as a key development issue in Vision 2030 was an oversight failure. The 200-page Action Plan, developed with support from the <a href="/wiki/Climate_%26_Development_Knowledge_Network" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate &amp; Development Knowledge Network">Climate &amp; Development Knowledge Network</a>, sets out the Government of Kenya's vision for a 'low-carbon climate resilient development pathway'. At the launch in March 2013, the Secretary of the Ministry of Planning, National Development, and Vision 2030 emphasised that climate would be a central issue in the renewed Medium-Term Plan that would be launched in the coming months. This would create a direct and robust delivery framework for the Action Plan and ensure climate change is treated as an economy-wide issue.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oil_exploration">Oil exploration</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Kenya#Petroleum" title="Energy in Kenya">Oil in Kenya</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kenya_Aerial_2009-08-27_14-26-44.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Kenya_Aerial_2009-08-27_14-26-44.JPG/220px-Kenya_Aerial_2009-08-27_14-26-44.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Kenya_Aerial_2009-08-27_14-26-44.JPG/330px-Kenya_Aerial_2009-08-27_14-26-44.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Kenya_Aerial_2009-08-27_14-26-44.JPG/440px-Kenya_Aerial_2009-08-27_14-26-44.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4253" data-file-height="2825"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kenya_Aerial_2009-08-27_14-26-44.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Lake_Turkana" title="Lake Turkana">Lake Turkana</a> borders Turkana County
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Kenya has proven oil deposits in <a href="/wiki/Turkana_County" title="Turkana County">Turkana County</a>. President Mwai Kibaki announced on 26 March 2012 that <a href="/wiki/Tullow_Oil" title="Tullow Oil">Tullow Oil</a>, an Anglo-Irish oil exploration firm, had struck oil, but its commercial viability and subsequent production would take about three years to confirm.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Early in 2006, Chinese president <a href="/wiki/Hu_Jintao" title="Hu Jintao">Hu Jintao</a> signed an oil exploration contract with Kenya, part of a series of deals designed to keep Africa's natural resources flowing to China's rapidly expanding economy. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Lions_Family_Portrait_Masai_Mara.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Lions_Family_Portrait_Masai_Mara.jpg/220px-Lions_Family_Portrait_Masai_Mara.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Lions_Family_Portrait_Masai_Mara.jpg/330px-Lions_Family_Portrait_Masai_Mara.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Lions_Family_Portrait_Masai_Mara.jpg/440px-Lions_Family_Portrait_Masai_Mara.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Lions_Family_Portrait_Masai_Mara.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Lions Family Portrait Masai Mara
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The deal allowed for China's state-controlled offshore oil and gas company, <a href="/wiki/China_National_Offshore_Oil_Corporation" title="China National Offshore Oil Corporation">CNOOC</a>, to prospect for oil in Kenya, which is just beginning to drill its first exploratory wells on the borders of Sudan and the disputed area of <a href="/wiki/North_Eastern_Province,_Kenya" class="mw-redirect" title="North Eastern Province, Kenya">North Eastern Province</a>, on the border with <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a> and in coastal waters. There are formal estimates of the possible reserves of oil discovered.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Child_labour_and_prostitution">Child labour and prostitution</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Enfants_Masai_-_Kenya_d%C3%A9cembre_1990.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Enfants_Masai_-_Kenya_d%C3%A9cembre_1990.jpg/220px-Enfants_Masai_-_Kenya_d%C3%A9cembre_1990.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Enfants_Masai_-_Kenya_d%C3%A9cembre_1990.jpg/330px-Enfants_Masai_-_Kenya_d%C3%A9cembre_1990.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Enfants_Masai_-_Kenya_d%C3%A9cembre_1990.jpg/440px-Enfants_Masai_-_Kenya_d%C3%A9cembre_1990.jpg 2x" data-file-width="855" data-file-height="580"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Enfants_Masai_-_Kenya_d%C3%A9cembre_1990.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Maasai_people" title="Maasai people">Maasai people</a>. The Maasai live in both Kenya and Tanzania.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Child labour is common in Kenya. Most working children are active in agriculture.<sup id="cite_ref-Country_profile_report_–_Kenya_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Country_profile_report_–_Kenya-176">[176]</a></sup> In 2006, UNICEF estimated that up to 30% of girls in the coastal areas of Malindi, Mombasa, Kilifi, and Diani were subject to prostitution. Most of the prostitutes in Kenya are aged 9–18.<sup id="cite_ref-Country_profile_report_–_Kenya_176-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Country_profile_report_–_Kenya-176">[176]</a></sup> The Ministry of Gender and Child Affairs employed 400 child protection officers in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-Country_profile_report_–_Kenya_176-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Country_profile_report_–_Kenya-176">[176]</a></sup> The causes of child labour include poverty, the lack of access to education, and weak government institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-Country_profile_report_–_Kenya_176-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Country_profile_report_–_Kenya-176">[176]</a></sup> Kenya has ratified Convention No. 81 on labour inspection in industries and Convention No. 129 on labour inspection in agriculture.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:African_Kids_working_in_the_family_farm.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/African_Kids_working_in_the_family_farm.jpg/220px-African_Kids_working_in_the_family_farm.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/African_Kids_working_in_the_family_farm.jpg/330px-African_Kids_working_in_the_family_farm.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/African_Kids_working_in_the_family_farm.jpg/440px-African_Kids_working_in_the_family_farm.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1080"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:African_Kids_working_in_the_family_farm.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Child labour in Kenya
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Microfinance_in_Kenya">Microfinance in Kenya</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Microfinance_in_Kenya" title="Microfinance in Kenya">Microfinance in Kenya</a>
      </div> 
      <p>24 institutions offer business loans on a large scale, specific agriculture loans, education loans, and loans for all other purposes. Additionally, there are: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>emergency loans, which are more expensive in respect to interest rates, but are quickly available</li> 
       <li>group loans for smaller groups (4–5 members) and larger groups (up to 30 members)</li> 
       <li>women's loans, which are also available to groups of women</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Out of approximately 40 million <a href="/wiki/Kenyans" class="mw-redirect" title="Kenyans">Kenyans</a>, about 14 million are not able to receive financial service through formal loan application services, and an additional 12 million have no access to financial service institutions at all. Further, 1 million Kenyans are reliant on informal groups for receiving financial aid.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><b>Conditions for microfinance products</b> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Eligibility criteria: the general criteria might include gender as in the case of special women's loans; being at least 18 years old; owning a valid Kenyan ID; having a business; demonstrating the ability to repay the loan; and being a customer of the institution.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Credit_scoring" class="mw-redirect" title="Credit scoring">Credit scoring</a>: there is no advanced credit scoring system and the majority has not stated any official loan distribution system. However, some institutions require applicants to have an existing business for at least 3 months, own a small amount of cash, provide the institution with a business plan or proposal, have at least one <a href="/wiki/Guarantor" class="mw-redirect" title="Guarantor">guarantor</a>, or to attend group meetings or training. For group loans, almost half of the institutions require group members to guarantee for each other.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Interest_rate" title="Interest rate">Interest rate</a>: mostly calculated on a flat basis and some at a declining balance. More than 90% of the institutions require monthly interest payments. The average interest rate is 30–40% for loans up to KSh500,000. For loans above KSh500,000, interest rates go up to 71%.</li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Kenya" title="Demographics of Kenya">Demographics of Kenya</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kikuyu_woman_traditional_dress.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Kikuyu_woman_traditional_dress.jpg/170px-Kikuyu_woman_traditional_dress.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Kikuyu_woman_traditional_dress.jpg/255px-Kikuyu_woman_traditional_dress.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Kikuyu_woman_traditional_dress.jpg/340px-Kikuyu_woman_traditional_dress.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kikuyu_woman_traditional_dress.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu</a> <a href="/wiki/Kikuyu_people" title="Kikuyu people">Kikuyu</a> woman in traditional attire
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin-left: 10px"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th colspan="4" style="text-align:center; background:#cfb;">Population<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-179">[179]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-180">[180]</a></sup> </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <th style="background:#cfb;">Year </th> 
         <th style="background:#cfb;">Million </th>

         <td style="text-align:right;">6.1 </td>
        </tr>

         <td style="text-align:left;">2000</td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">31.4 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:left;">2018</td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">51.4 </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Kenya had a population of approximately 48 million people in January 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_11-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-11">[11]</a></sup> The country has a young population, with 73% of residents aged below 30 years because of rapid <a href="/wiki/Population_growth" title="Population growth">population growth</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> from 2.9&nbsp;million to 40&nbsp;million inhabitants over the last century.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kenya's capital, Nairobi, is home to <a href="/wiki/Kibera" title="Kibera">Kibera</a>, one of the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Shanty_town" title="Shanty town">slums</a>. The shantytown is believed to house between 170,000<sup id="cite_ref-nation1_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nation1-184">[184]</a></sup> and 1 million people.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> The UNHCR base in <a href="/wiki/Dadaab" title="Dadaab">Dadaab</a> in the north also currently houses around 500,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-DadaabPop_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DadaabPop-186">[186]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span></h3> 
      <p>Kenya has a diverse population that includes many of the major ethnoracial and linguistic groups found in Africa. Although there is no official list of Kenyan ethnic groups, the number of ethnic categories and sub-categories recorded in the country's census has changed significantly over time, expanding from 42 in 1969, to more than 120 in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-Balaton-Chrimes2020_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Balaton-Chrimes2020-187">[187]</a></sup> The majority of local resident are made up of <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantus</a> (60%) and <a href="/wiki/Nilotic_peoples" title="Nilotic peoples">Nilotes</a> (30%).<sup id="cite_ref-Asongumarr_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Asongumarr-188">[188]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cushitic_languages" title="Cushitic languages">Cushitic</a> groups also form a small <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_minority" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic minority">ethnic minority</a>, as do <a href="/wiki/Arab" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab">Arabs</a>, Indians, and Europeans.<sup id="cite_ref-Asongumarr_188-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Asongumarr-188">[188]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Okothndaloh_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Okothndaloh-189">[189]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Kenya_National_Bureau_of_Statistics" title="Kenya National Bureau of Statistics">Kenya National Bureau of Statistics</a> (KNBS), In 2019, Kenya had a total population of 47,564,296 inhabitants. The largest native ethnic groups were the <a href="/wiki/Kikuyu_people" title="Kikuyu people">Kikuyu</a> (8,148,668), <a href="/wiki/Luhya_people" title="Luhya people">Luhya</a> (6,823,842), <a href="/wiki/Kalenjin_people" title="Kalenjin people">Kalenjin</a> (6,358,113), <a href="/wiki/Luo_people" title="Luo people">Luo</a> (5,066,966), <a href="/wiki/Kamba_people" title="Kamba people">Kamba</a> (4,663,910), <a href="/wiki/Somalis" title="Somalis">Somalis</a> (2,780,502), <a href="/wiki/Kisii_people" title="Kisii people">Kisii</a> (2,703,235), <a href="/wiki/Mijikenda_peoples" title="Mijikenda peoples">Mijikenda</a> (2,488,691), <a href="/wiki/Meru_people" title="Meru people">Meru</a> (1,975,869), <a href="/wiki/Maasai_people" title="Maasai people">Maasai</a> (1,189,522), and <a href="/wiki/Turkana_people" title="Turkana people">Turkana</a> (1,016,174). The <a href="/wiki/North_Eastern_Province,_Kenya" class="mw-redirect" title="North Eastern Province, Kenya">North Eastern Province</a> of Kenya, formerly known as NFD, is predominantly inhabited by the indigenous ethnic <a href="/wiki/Somalis" title="Somalis">Somalis</a>. Foreign-rooted populations include <a href="/wiki/Somalis" title="Somalis">Somalis</a> (from <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>), <a href="/wiki/Omanis" class="mw-redirect" title="Omanis">Arabs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indians_in_Kenya" title="Indians in Kenya">Asians</a>, and <a href="/wiki/White_people_in_Kenya" title="White people in Kenya">Europeans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Census2019a_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census2019a-2">[2]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Kenya" title="Languages of Kenya">Languages of Kenya</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Kenya's various ethnic groups typically speak their <a href="/wiki/Mother_tongue" class="mw-redirect" title="Mother tongue">mother tongues</a> within their own communities. The two <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official languages</a>, English and <a href="/wiki/Swahili_language" title="Swahili language">Swahili</a>, are used in varying degrees of fluency for communication with other populations. English is widely spoken in commerce, schooling, and government.<sup id="cite_ref-Cugrwed_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cugrwed-190">[190]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Peri-urbanisation" title="Peri-urbanisation">Peri-urban</a> and rural dwellers are less multilingual, with many in rural areas speaking only their native languages.<sup id="cite_ref-Broassim_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Broassim-191">[191]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">British English</a> is primarily used in Kenya. Additionally, a distinct local dialect, <a href="/wiki/Kenyan_English" title="Kenyan English">Kenyan English</a>, is used by some communities and individuals in the country, and contains features unique to it that were derived from local <a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">Bantu languages</a> such as Kiswahili and <a href="/wiki/Gikuyu_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Gikuyu language">Kikuyu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Cliike_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cliike-192">[192]</a></sup> It has been developing since colonisation and also contains certain elements of <a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">American English</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sheng_slang" title="Sheng slang">Sheng</a> is a Kiswahili-based <a href="/wiki/Cant_(language)" title="Cant (language)">cant</a> spoken in some urban areas. Primarily consisting of a mixture of Kiswahili and English, it is an example of linguistic <a href="/wiki/Code-switching" title="Code-switching">code-switching</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Nphil_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nphil-193">[193]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are a total of 69 languages spoken in Kenya. Most belong to two broad language families: <a href="/wiki/Niger-Congo_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Niger-Congo languages">Niger-Congo</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">Bantu branch</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Nilo-Saharan_languages" title="Nilo-Saharan languages">Nilo-Saharan</a> (<a href="/wiki/Nilotic_languages" title="Nilotic languages">Nilotic branch</a>), spoken by the country's Bantu and Nilotic populations respectively. The Cushitic and Arab ethnic minorities speak languages belonging to the separate <a href="/wiki/Afroasiatic_languages" title="Afroasiatic languages">Afroasiatic</a> family, with the Indian and European residents speaking languages from the <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">Indo-European</a> family.<sup id="cite_ref-Ethnken_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ethnken-194">[194]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_centres">Urban centres</span></h3>

       Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_in_Kenya_by_population" title="List of cities and towns in Kenya by population">List of cities and towns in Kenya by population</a>
      </div>

         <td rowspan="11" style="text-align: center"><a href="/wiki/File:NBO5.jpg" class="image" title="Nairobi"><img alt="Nairobi" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/NBO5.jpg/120px-NBO5.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="90" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/NBO5.jpg/180px-NBO5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/NBO5.jpg/240px-NBO5.jpg 2x" data-file-width="804" data-file-height="606"></a><br><a href="/wiki/Nairobi" title="Nairobi">Nairobi</a><br><a href="/wiki/File:Wooden_boat_off-shore_in_Mombasa%27s_Marine_Park.jpg" class="image" title="Mombasa"><img alt="Mombasa" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Wooden_boat_off-shore_in_Mombasa%27s_Marine_Park.jpg/120px-Wooden_boat_off-shore_in_Mombasa%27s_Marine_Park.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="80" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Wooden_boat_off-shore_in_Mombasa%27s_Marine_Park.jpg/180px-Wooden_boat_off-shore_in_Mombasa%27s_Marine_Park.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Wooden_boat_off-shore_in_Mombasa%27s_Marine_Park.jpg/240px-Wooden_boat_off-shore_in_Mombasa%27s_Marine_Park.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1365"></a><br><a href="/wiki/Mombasa" title="Mombasa">Mombasa</a> </td>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Kenya" title="Religion in Kenya">Religion in Kenya</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Catholic_Church_in_Mombasa.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Catholic_Church_in_Mombasa.JPG/220px-Catholic_Church_in_Mombasa.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Catholic_Church_in_Mombasa.JPG/330px-Catholic_Church_in_Mombasa.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Catholic_Church_in_Mombasa.JPG/440px-Catholic_Church_in_Mombasa.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Catholic_Church_in_Mombasa.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Holy Ghost Roman Catholic Cathedral in Mombasa.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The majority of Kenyans are <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christian</a> (85.5%), of whom 53.9% are <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> and 20.6% are <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_in_Kenya" title="Catholic Church in Kenya">Roman Catholic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Census2019a_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census2019a-2">[2]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Church_of_East_Africa" title="Presbyterian Church of East Africa">Presbyterian Church of East Africa</a> has 3 million followers in Kenya and surrounding countries.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> There are smaller conservative <a href="/wiki/Reformed" class="mw-redirect" title="Reformed">Reformed</a> churches, the <a href="/wiki/Africa_Evangelical_Presbyterian_Church" title="Africa Evangelical Presbyterian Church">Africa Evangelical Presbyterian Church</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Independent_Presbyterian_Church_in_Kenya" title="Independent Presbyterian Church in Kenya">Independent Presbyterian Church in Kenya</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Reformed_Church_of_East_Africa" title="Reformed Church of East Africa">Reformed Church of East Africa</a>. <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Christianity" class="mw-redirect" title="Orthodox Christianity">Orthodox Christianity</a> counts 621,200 adherents.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> Kenya has by far the highest number of <a href="/wiki/Quaker" class="mw-redirect" title="Quaker">Quakers</a> of any country in the world, with around 146,300 members.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> The only <a href="/wiki/Jewish_synagogue" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish synagogue">Jewish synagogue</a> in the country is located in Nairobi. </p>
      <p>Islam is the <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Kenya" title="Islam in Kenya">second largest religion</a>, comprising 10.9% of the population. Sixty percent of Kenyan Muslims live in the <a href="/wiki/Coast_Province" title="Coast Province">Coastal Region</a>, comprising 50% of the total population there, while the upper part of Kenya's <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Province_(Kenya)" title="Eastern Province (Kenya)">Eastern Region</a> is home to 10% of the country's Muslims, where they constitute the majority religious group.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/African_traditional_religion" class="mw-redirect" title="African traditional religion">Indigenous beliefs</a> are practised by 0.7% of the population, although many self-identifying Christians and Muslims <a href="/wiki/Religious_syncretism" title="Religious syncretism">maintain some traditional beliefs and customs</a>. Nonreligious Kenyans make up 1.6% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-Census2019a_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census2019a-2">[2]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are Hindus living in Kenya. The numbers are estimated to be around 60,287 people or 0.13% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-Census2019a_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census2019a-2">[2]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Kenya" title="Health in Kenya">Health in Kenya</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kapsowarhospital1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Kapsowarhospital1.jpg/220px-Kapsowarhospital1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Kapsowarhospital1.jpg/330px-Kapsowarhospital1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Kapsowarhospital1.jpg/440px-Kapsowarhospital1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2048"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kapsowarhospital1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Outpatient Department of AIC Kapsowar Hospital<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Kapsowar" title="Kapsowar">Kapsowar</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Private health facilities are diverse, highly dynamic, and difficult to classify, unlike public health facilities, which are easily grouped in classes that consist of community-based (level I) services, run by <a href="/wiki/Community_health" title="Community health">community health</a> workers; dispensaries (level II facilities) run by <a href="/wiki/Nurse" class="mw-redirect" title="Nurse">nurses</a>; health centers (level III facilities), run by <a href="/wiki/Clinical_officer" title="Clinical officer">clinical officers</a>; sub-county hospitals (level IV facilities), which may be run by a <a href="/wiki/Clinical_officer" title="Clinical officer">clinical officer</a> or a <a href="/wiki/General_practitioner" title="General practitioner">medical officer</a>; county hospitals (level V facilities), which may be run by a <a href="/wiki/General_practitioner" title="General practitioner">medical officer</a> or a <a href="/wiki/Consultant_(medicine)" title="Consultant (medicine)">medical practitioner</a>; and national referral hospitals (level VI facilities), which are run by fully qualified <a href="/wiki/Consultant_(medicine)" title="Consultant (medicine)">medical practitioners</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Table_rco_co_mo_medical_practitioners.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Table_rco_co_mo_medical_practitioners.png/220px-Table_rco_co_mo_medical_practitioners.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="58" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Table_rco_co_mo_medical_practitioners.png/330px-Table_rco_co_mo_medical_practitioners.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Table_rco_co_mo_medical_practitioners.png/440px-Table_rco_co_mo_medical_practitioners.png 2x" data-file-width="1218" data-file-height="323"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Table_rco_co_mo_medical_practitioners.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Table showing different grades of clinical officers, medical officers, and medical practitioners in Kenya's public service
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Nurses" class="mw-redirect" title="Nurses">Nurses</a> are by far the largest group of <a href="/wiki/Front-line" class="mw-redirect" title="Front-line">front-line</a> health care providers in all sectors, followed by <a href="/wiki/Clinical_officer" title="Clinical officer">clinical officers</a>, <a href="/wiki/General_practitioner" title="General practitioner">medical officers</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Consultant_(medicine)" title="Consultant (medicine)">medical practitioners</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/Kenya_National_Bureau_of_Statistics" title="Kenya National Bureau of Statistics">Kenya National Bureau of Statistics</a>, in 2011 there were 65,000 qualified nurses registered in the country, 8,600 clinical officers, and 7,000 doctors, for the population of 43 million people (these figures from official registers include those who have died or left the profession, hence the actual number of these workers may be lower).<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Traditional_healer" class="mw-redirect" title="Traditional healer">Traditional healers</a> (<a href="/wiki/Herbalist" class="mw-redirect" title="Herbalist">herbalists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Witch_doctor" title="Witch doctor">witch doctors</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Faith_healer" class="mw-redirect" title="Faith healer">faith healers</a>) are readily available, trusted, and widely consulted as practitioners of first or last choice by both rural and urban dwellers. </p>
      <p>Despite major achievements in the health sector, Kenya still faces many challenges. The estimated <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> dropped in 2009 to approximately 55 years — five years below the 1990 level.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality" title="Infant mortality">infant mortality</a> rate was high at approximately 44 deaths per 1,000 children in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> The WHO estimated in 2011 that only 42% of births were attended by a skilled health professional.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Diseases_of_poverty" title="Diseases of poverty">Diseases of poverty</a> directly correlate with a country's <a href="/wiki/Economy" title="Economy">economic performance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wealth_distribution" class="mw-redirect" title="Wealth distribution">wealth distribution</a>: Half of Kenyans live below the poverty level. Preventable diseases like malaria, HIV/AIDS, pneumonia, diarrhoea, and malnutrition are the biggest burden, major child-killers, and responsible for much morbidity; weak policies, corruption, inadequate health workers, weak management, and poor leadership in the public health sector are largely to blame. According to 2009 estimates, <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_HIV/AIDS_adult_prevalence_rate" title="List of countries by HIV/AIDS adult prevalence rate">HIV/AIDS prevalence</a> is about 6.3% of the adult population.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup> However, the 2011 UNAIDS Report suggests that the HIV epidemic may be improving in Kenya, as HIV prevalence is declining among young people (ages 15–24) and pregnant women.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup> Kenya had an estimated 15 million cases of <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a> in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Women">Women</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Women_in_Kenya" title="Women in Kenya">Women in Kenya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Child_marriage_in_Kenya" title="Child marriage in Kenya">Child marriage in Kenya</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Polygamy_in_Kenya" title="Polygamy in Kenya">Polygamy in Kenya</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kenyan_Women_in_Nairobi_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Kenyan_Women_in_Nairobi_01.jpg/220px-Kenyan_Women_in_Nairobi_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="192" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Kenyan_Women_in_Nairobi_01.jpg/330px-Kenyan_Women_in_Nairobi_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Kenyan_Women_in_Nairobi_01.jpg/440px-Kenyan_Women_in_Nairobi_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2600" data-file-height="2269"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kenyan_Women_in_Nairobi_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Kenyan women in Nairobi
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> in Kenya was estimated to be 4.49 children per woman in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> According to a 2008–09 survey by the Kenyan government, the total fertility rate was 4.6% and the contraception usage rate among married women was 46%.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Maternal_mortality" class="mw-redirect" title="Maternal mortality">Maternal mortality</a> is high, partly because of <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_cutting" class="mw-redirect" title="Female genital cutting">female genital mutilation</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-lcweb2.loc.gov_148-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lcweb2.loc.gov-148">[148]</a></sup> with about 27% of women having undergone it.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> This practice is however on the decline as the country becomes more modernised, and in 2011 it was banned in Kenya.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> Women were economically empowered before colonialisation. By colonial land alienation, women lost access and control of land.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-213">[213]</a></sup> They became more economically dependent on men.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_213-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-213">[213]</a></sup> A colonial order of gender emerged where males dominated females.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_213-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-213">[213]</a></sup> Median age at first marriage increases with increasing education.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> Rape, defilement, and battering are not always seen as serious crimes.<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-215">[215]</a></sup> Reports of sexual assault are not always taken seriously.<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_215-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-215">[215]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Kenya" title="Education in Kenya">Education in Kenya</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Community_work_in_Kenya_DVIDS342488.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Community_work_in_Kenya_DVIDS342488.jpg/220px-Community_work_in_Kenya_DVIDS342488.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Community_work_in_Kenya_DVIDS342488.jpg/330px-Community_work_in_Kenya_DVIDS342488.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Community_work_in_Kenya_DVIDS342488.jpg/440px-Community_work_in_Kenya_DVIDS342488.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="1500"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Community_work_in_Kenya_DVIDS342488.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>School children in a classroom.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:MSc_student_at_Kenyatta_University.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/MSc_student_at_Kenyatta_University.jpg/220px-MSc_student_at_Kenyatta_University.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/MSc_student_at_Kenyatta_University.jpg/330px-MSc_student_at_Kenyatta_University.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/MSc_student_at_Kenyatta_University.jpg/440px-MSc_student_at_Kenyatta_University.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:MSc_student_at_Kenyatta_University.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>An MSc student at <a href="/wiki/Kenyatta_University" title="Kenyatta University">Kenyatta University</a> in Nairobi.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Children attend nursery school, or kindergarten in the private sector until they are five years old. This lasts one to three years (KG1, KG2 and KG3) and is financed privately because there has been no government policy on pre-schooling until recently.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Basic formal education starts at age six and lasts 12 years, consisting of eight years in primary school and four in high school or secondary. Primary school is free in public schools and those attending can join a vocational youth/village polytechnic, or make their own arrangements for an apprenticeship program and learn a trade such as tailoring, carpentry, motor vehicle repair, brick-laying and masonry for about two years.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-217">[217]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Those who complete high school can join a <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_technology" title="Institute of technology">polytechnic</a> or other technical college and study for three years, or proceed directly to university and study for four years. Graduates from the polytechnics and colleges can then join the workforce and later obtain a specialised higher diploma qualification after a further one to two years of training, or join the university—usually in the second or third year of their respective course. The <a href="/wiki/Higher_diploma" title="Higher diploma">higher diploma</a> is accepted by many employers in place of a bachelor's degree and direct or accelerated admission to post-graduate studies is possible in some universities. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Masai_girl_at_school_doing_maths.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Masai_girl_at_school_doing_maths.jpg/220px-Masai_girl_at_school_doing_maths.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Masai_girl_at_school_doing_maths.jpg/330px-Masai_girl_at_school_doing_maths.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Masai_girl_at_school_doing_maths.jpg/440px-Masai_girl_at_school_doing_maths.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="886"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Masai_girl_at_school_doing_maths.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A Maasai girl at school.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Public universities in Kenya are highly commercialised institutions and only a small fraction of qualified high school graduates are admitted on limited government-sponsorship into programs of their choice. Most are admitted into the social sciences, which are cheap to run, or as self-sponsored students paying the full cost of their studies. Most qualified students who miss out opt for middle-level diploma programs in public or private universities, colleges, and polytechnics. </p>
      <p>In 2018, 18.5 percent of the Kenyan adult population was illiterate, which was the highest rate of literacy in East Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup> There are very wide regional disparities: for example, Nairobi had the highest level of literacy at 87.1 per cent, compared to North Eastern Province, the lowest, at 8.0 per cent. Preschool, which targets children from age three to five, is an integral component of the education system and is a key requirement for admission to Standard One (First Grade). At the end of primary education, pupils sit the <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Certificate_of_Primary_Education" title="Kenya Certificate of Primary Education">Kenya Certificate of Primary Education</a> (KCPE), which determines those who proceed to secondary school or vocational training. The result of this examination is needed for placement at secondary school.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_217-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-217">[217]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Primary school is for students aged 6/7-13/14 years. For those who proceed to the secondary level, there is a national examination at the end of Form Four&nbsp;– the <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Certificate_of_Secondary_Education" title="Kenya Certificate of Secondary Education">Kenya Certificate of Secondary Education</a> (KCSE), which determines those proceeding to the universities, other professional training, or employment. Students sit <a href="/wiki/Examinations" class="mw-redirect" title="Examinations">examinations</a> in eight subjects of their choosing. However, English, Kiswahili, and mathematics are compulsory subjects. </p>
      <p>The Kenya Universities and Colleges Central Placement Service (KUCCPS), formerly the Joint Admissions Board (JAB), is responsible for selecting students joining the public universities. Other than the public schools, there are many private schools, mainly in urban areas. Similarly, there are a number of <a href="/wiki/International_school" title="International school">international schools</a> catering to various overseas educational systems. </p>
      <p>Despite its impressive commercial approach and interests in the country, Kenya's <a href="/wiki/Academia" class="mw-redirect" title="Academia">academia</a> and higher education system is notoriously rigid and disconnected from the needs of the local labour market and is widely blamed for the high number of unemployable and "half-baked" university graduates who struggle to fit in the modern workplace.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>

      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Kenya" title="Culture of Kenya">Culture of Kenya</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kenyan_dancers.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Kenyan_dancers.jpg/220px-Kenyan_dancers.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Kenyan_dancers.jpg/330px-Kenyan_dancers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Kenyan_dancers.jpg/440px-Kenyan_dancers.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1384" data-file-height="1089"></a>

          <a href="/wiki/File:Kenyan_dancers.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
