        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nation_media_house.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Nation_media_house.jpg/220px-Nation_media_house.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Nation_media_house.jpg/330px-Nation_media_house.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Nation_media_house.jpg/440px-Nation_media_house.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="851"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nation_media_house.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Nation Media House, which hosts the <a href="/wiki/Nation_Media_Group" title="Nation Media Group">Nation Media Group</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Kenya" title="Culture of Kenya">culture of Kenya</a> consists of multiple traditions. Kenya has no single prominent culture that identifies it. It instead consists of the various cultures of the country's different communities. </p>
      <p>Notable populations include the <a href="/wiki/Swahili_people" title="Swahili people">Swahili</a> on the coast, several other <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu</a> communities in the central and western regions, and Nilotic communities in the northwest. The <a href="/wiki/Maasai_people" title="Maasai people">Maasai</a> culture is well known to tourism, despite constituting a relatively small part of Kenya's population. They are renowned for their elaborate upper-body adornment and jewellery. </p>
      <p>Additionally, Kenya has an extensive music, television, and theatre scene. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Kenya" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of Kenya">Media of Kenya</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Kenya has a number of media outlets that broadcast domestically and globally. They cover news, business, sports, and entertainment. Popular Kenyan newspapers include: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Nation" title="Daily Nation">The Daily Nation</a></i>; part of the <a href="/wiki/Nation_Media_Group" title="Nation Media Group">Nation Media Group (NMG)</a> (largest market share)</li> 
       <li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Standard_(Kenya)" title="The Standard (Kenya)">The Standard</a></i></li> 
       <li><i>The Star</i></li> 
       <li><i>The People</i></li> 
       <li><i>East Africa Weekly</i></li> 
       <li><i><a href="/wiki/Taifa_Leo" title="Taifa Leo">Taifa Leo</a></i></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Television stations based in Kenya include: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Kenya_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Kenya Broadcasting Corporation">Kenya Broadcasting Corporation</a> (KBC)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Citizen_TV" title="Citizen TV">Citizen TV</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Kenya_Television_Network" title="Kenya Television Network">Kenya Television Network</a> (KTN)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/NTV_(Kenya)" class="mw-redirect" title="NTV (Kenya)">NTV</a> (part of the <a href="/wiki/Nation_Media_Group" title="Nation Media Group">Nation Media Group</a> (NMG))</li> 
       <li>Kiss Television</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/K24_(Kenya)" class="mw-redirect" title="K24 (Kenya)">K24 Television</a></li> 
       <li>Kass-TV</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>All of these terrestrial channels are transmitted via a DVB T2 digital TV signal. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kenyan_literature" title="Kenyan literature">Kenyan literature</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ng%C5%A9g%C4%A9_wa_Thiong%27o_(signing_autographs_in_London).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Ng%C5%A9g%C4%A9_wa_Thiong%27o_%28signing_autographs_in_London%29.jpg/220px-Ng%C5%A9g%C4%A9_wa_Thiong%27o_%28signing_autographs_in_London%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="181" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Ng%C5%A9g%C4%A9_wa_Thiong%27o_%28signing_autographs_in_London%29.jpg/330px-Ng%C5%A9g%C4%A9_wa_Thiong%27o_%28signing_autographs_in_London%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Ng%C5%A9g%C4%A9_wa_Thiong%27o_%28signing_autographs_in_London%29.jpg/440px-Ng%C5%A9g%C4%A9_wa_Thiong%27o_%28signing_autographs_in_London%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="591" data-file-height="485"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ng%C5%A9g%C4%A9_wa_Thiong%27o_(signing_autographs_in_London).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Kenyan author <a href="/wiki/Ng%C5%A9g%C4%A9_wa_Thiong%27o" title="Ngũgĩ wa Thiong'o">Ngũgĩ wa Thiong'o</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Ng%C5%A9g%C4%A9_wa_Thiong%27o" title="Ngũgĩ wa Thiong'o">Ngũgĩ wa Thiong'o</a> is one of the best known writers in Kenya. His novel, <i><a href="/wiki/Weep_Not,_Child" title="Weep Not, Child">Weep Not, Child</a></i>, is an illustration of life in Kenya during the British occupation. The story details the effects of the Mau Mau on the lives of Kenyans. Its combination of themes—<a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonialism</a>, education, and love—helped to make it one of the best-known novels in Africa. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/M.G._Vassanji" class="mw-redirect" title="M.G. Vassanji">M.G. Vassanji</a>'s 2003 novel <i>The In-Between World of Vikram Lall</i> won the <a href="/wiki/Scotiabank_Giller_Prize" class="mw-redirect" title="Scotiabank Giller Prize">Giller Prize</a> in 2003. It is the fictional memoir of a Kenyan of Indian heritage and his family as they adjust to the changing political climates in colonial and post-colonial Kenya. </p>
      <p>Since 2003, the literary journal <i><a href="/wiki/Kwani%3F" title="Kwani?">Kwani?</a></i> has been publishing Kenyan contemporary literature. Additionally, Kenya has also been nurturing emerging versatile authors such as Paul Kipchumba (Kipwendui, Kibiwott) who demonstrate a pan-African outlook (see <i>Africa in China's 21st Century: In Search of a Strategy</i> (2017).<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Kenya" title="Music of Kenya">Music of Kenya</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Juacali_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Juacali_2.jpg/220px-Juacali_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Juacali_2.jpg/330px-Juacali_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Juacali_2.jpg/440px-Juacali_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2736" data-file-height="3648"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Juacali_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Popular Kenyan musician <a href="/wiki/Jua_Cali" title="Jua Cali">Jua Cali</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Kenya has a diverse assortment of popular music forms, in addition to multiple types of <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">folk music</a> based on the variety of over 40 regional languages.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Drums are the most dominant <a href="/wiki/Musical_instrument" title="Musical instrument">instrument</a> in popular Kenyan music. Drum beats are very complex and include both native rhythms and imported ones, especially the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Congolese</a> <a href="/wiki/Cavacha" title="Cavacha">cavacha</a> rhythm. Popular Kenyan music usually involves the interplay of multiple parts, and more recently, showy guitar solos as well. There are also a number of local hip-hop artists, including <a href="/wiki/Jua_Cali" title="Jua Cali">Jua Cali</a>; Afro-pop bands such as <a href="/wiki/Sauti_Sol" title="Sauti Sol">Sauti Sol</a>; and musicians who play local genres like Benga, such as <a href="/wiki/Akothee" title="Akothee">Akothee</a>. </p>
      <p>Lyrics are most often in Kiswahili or English. There is also some emerging aspect of <a href="/wiki/Lingala_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Lingala language">Lingala</a> borrowed from <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Congolese</a> musicians. Lyrics are also written in local languages. Urban radio generally only plays English music, though there also exist a number of vernacular radio stations. </p>
      <p>Zilizopendwa is a genre of local urban music that was recorded in the 1960s, 70s, and 80s by musicians such as <a href="/wiki/Daudi_Kabaka" title="Daudi Kabaka">Daudi Kabaka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fadhili_William" title="Fadhili William">Fadhili William</a>, and Sukuma Bin Ongaro, and is particularly enjoyed by older people—having been popularised by the Kenya Broadcasting Corporation's Kiswahili service (formerly called Voice of Kenya or VOK). </p>
      <p>The Isukuti is a vigorous dance performed by the <a href="/wiki/Luhya_people" title="Luhya people">Luhya</a> sub-tribes to the beat of a traditional drum called the Isukuti during many occasions such as the birth of a child, marriage, or funeral. Other traditional dances include the <a href="/wiki/Ohangla" title="Ohangla">Ohangla</a> among the <a href="/wiki/Luo_peoples" title="Luo peoples">Luo</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nzele&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nzele (page does not exist)">Nzele</a> among the <a href="/wiki/Mijikenda_peoples" title="Mijikenda peoples">Mijikenda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mugithi" title="Mugithi">Mugithi</a> among the <a href="/wiki/Kikuyu_people" title="Kikuyu people">Kikuyu</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Taarab" title="Taarab">Taarab</a> among the <a href="/wiki/Swahili_people" title="Swahili people">Swahili</a>. </p>
      <p>Additionally, Kenya has a growing Christian gospel music scene. Prominent local gospel musicians include the <a href="/wiki/Kenyan_Boys_Choir" title="Kenyan Boys Choir">Kenyan Boys Choir</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Benga_music" title="Benga music">Benga music</a> has been popular since the late 1960s, especially in the area around <a href="/wiki/Lake_Victoria" title="Lake Victoria">Lake Victoria</a>. The word <i>benga</i> is occasionally used to refer to any kind of pop music. Bass, guitar, and percussion are the usual instruments. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Kenya" title="Sport in Kenya">Sport in Kenya</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2012_Olympics_-_Womens_5000m_start_4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/2012_Olympics_-_Womens_5000m_start_4.jpg/220px-2012_Olympics_-_Womens_5000m_start_4.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/2012_Olympics_-_Womens_5000m_start_4.jpg/330px-2012_Olympics_-_Womens_5000m_start_4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/2012_Olympics_-_Womens_5000m_start_4.jpg/440px-2012_Olympics_-_Womens_5000m_start_4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2012_Olympics_-_Womens_5000m_start_4.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Jepkosgei Kipyego and Jepkemoi Cheruiyot at the 2012 London Olympics
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Kenya is active in several sports, among them <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rallying" title="Rallying">rallying</a>, <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Field_hockey" title="Field hockey">field hockey</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a>. The country is known chiefly for its dominance in <a href="/wiki/Middle-distance_running" title="Middle-distance running">middle-distance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Long-distance_running" title="Long-distance running">long-distance</a> athletics, having consistently produced <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games" title="Commonwealth Games">Commonwealth Games</a> champions in various distance events, especially in 800&nbsp;m, 1,500&nbsp;m, 3,000&nbsp;m steeplechase, 5,000&nbsp;m, 10,000&nbsp;m, and the marathon. Kenyan athletes (particularly <a href="/wiki/Kalenjin_people" title="Kalenjin people">Kalenjin</a>), continue to dominate the world of distance running, although competition from <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a> has reduced this supremacy. Kenya's best-known athletes include the four-time women's <a href="/wiki/Boston_Marathon" title="Boston Marathon">Boston Marathon</a> winner and two-time world champion <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Ndereba" title="Catherine Ndereba">Catherine Ndereba</a>, 800m world record holder <a href="/wiki/David_Rudisha" title="David Rudisha">David Rudisha</a>, former <a href="/wiki/Marathon_(sport)" class="mw-redirect" title="Marathon (sport)">marathon</a> world record-holder <a href="/wiki/Paul_Tergat" title="Paul Tergat">Paul Tergat</a>, and <a href="/wiki/John_Ngugi" title="John Ngugi">John Ngugi</a>. </p>
      <p>Kenya won several medals during the Beijing Olympics: six gold, four silver, and four bronze, making it Africa's most successful nation in the 2008 Olympics. New athletes gained attention, such as <a href="/wiki/Pamela_Jelimo" title="Pamela Jelimo">Pamela Jelimo</a>, the women's 800m gold medalist who went on to win the <a href="/wiki/IAAF_Golden_League" title="IAAF Golden League">IAAF Golden League</a> jackpot, and <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Wanjiru" title="Samuel Wanjiru">Samuel Wanjiru</a>, who won the men's marathon. Retired Olympic and Commonwealth Games champion <a href="/wiki/Kipchoge_Keino" title="Kipchoge Keino">Kipchoge Keino</a> helped usher in Kenya's ongoing distance dynasty in the 1970s and was followed by Commonwealth Champion <a href="/wiki/Henry_Rono" title="Henry Rono">Henry Rono</a>'s spectacular string of world record performances. Lately, there has been controversy in Kenyan athletics circles, with the defection of a number of Kenyan athletes to represent other countries, chiefly <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IAAF_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IAAF-223">[223]</a></sup> The Kenyan Ministry of Sports has tried to stop the defections, but they have continued anyway, with <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Lagat" title="Bernard Lagat">Bernard Lagat</a> being the latest, choosing to represent the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-IAAF_223-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IAAF-223">[223]</a></sup> Most of these defections occur because of economic or financial factors.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup> Decisions by the Kenyan government to tax athletes' earnings may also be a motivating factor.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup> Some elite Kenyan runners who cannot qualify for their country's strong national team find it easier to qualify by running for other countries.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:David_Rudisha_Daegu_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/David_Rudisha_Daegu_2011.jpg/220px-David_Rudisha_Daegu_2011.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/David_Rudisha_Daegu_2011.jpg/330px-David_Rudisha_Daegu_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/David_Rudisha_Daegu_2011.jpg/440px-David_Rudisha_Daegu_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="426"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:David_Rudisha_Daegu_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Kenyan Olympic and world record holder in the 800 meters, <a href="/wiki/David_Rudisha" title="David Rudisha">David Rudisha</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Kenya has been a dominant force in women's volleyball within Africa, with both the clubs and the national team winning various continental championships in the past decade.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup> The women's team has competed at the Olympics and <a href="/wiki/FIVB_Volleyball_Women%27s_World_Championship" title="FIVB Volleyball Women's World Championship">World Championships</a>, though without any notable success. Cricket is another popular sport, also ranking as the most successful team sport. <a href="/wiki/Kenyan_cricket_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Kenyan cricket team">Kenya</a> has competed in the <a href="/wiki/Cricket_World_Cup" title="Cricket World Cup">Cricket World Cup</a> since <a href="/wiki/1996_Cricket_World_Cup" title="1996 Cricket World Cup">1996</a>. They upset some of the world's best teams and reached the semi-finals of the <a href="/wiki/2003_Cricket_World_Cup" title="2003 Cricket World Cup">2003 tournament</a>. They won the inaugural World Cricket League Division 1 hosted in Nairobi and participated in the World T20. They also participated in the <a href="/wiki/ICC_Cricket_World_Cup_2011" class="mw-redirect" title="ICC Cricket World Cup 2011">ICC Cricket World Cup 2011</a>. Their current captain is <a href="/wiki/Rakep_Patel" title="Rakep Patel">Rakep Patel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kenya is represented by <a href="/wiki/Lucas_Onyango" title="Lucas Onyango">Lucas Onyango</a> as a professional rugby league player who plays with the English club <a href="/wiki/Oldham_R.L.F.C." title="Oldham R.L.F.C.">Oldham</a>. Besides the former <a href="/wiki/Super_League" title="Super League">Super League</a> team, he has played for the <a href="/wiki/Widnes_Vikings" title="Widnes Vikings">Widnes Vikings</a> and with the <a href="/wiki/Sale_Sharks" title="Sale Sharks">Sale Sharks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup> Rugby is increasing in popularity, especially with the annual <a href="/w/index.php?title=Safaricom_Sevens&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Safaricom Sevens (page does not exist)">Safari Sevens</a> tournament. The <a href="/wiki/Kenya_national_rugby_sevens_team" title="Kenya national rugby sevens team">Kenya Sevens team</a> ranked 9th in the IRB Sevens World Series for the 2006 season. In 2016, the team beat Fiji at the Singapore Sevens finals, making Kenya the second African nation after South Africa to win a World Series championship.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kenya_national_football_team" title="Kenya national football team">Kenya</a> was once also a regional powerhouse in football. However, its dominance has been eroded by wrangles within the now defunct <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Football_Federation" class="mw-redirect" title="Kenya Football Federation">Kenya Football Federation</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup> leading to a suspension by <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> which was lifted in March 2007. </p>
      <p>In the motor rallying arena, Kenya is home to the world-famous <a href="/wiki/Safari_Rally" title="Safari Rally">Safari Rally</a>, commonly acknowledged as one of the toughest rallies in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup> It was a part of the <a href="/wiki/World_Rally_Championship" title="World Rally Championship">World Rally Championship</a> for many years until its exclusion after the 2002 event owing to financial difficulties. Some of the best rally drivers in the world have taken part in and won the rally, such as <a href="/wiki/Bj%C3%B6rn_Waldeg%C3%A5rd" title="Björn Waldegård">Björn Waldegård</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hannu_Mikkola" title="Hannu Mikkola">Hannu Mikkola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tommi_M%C3%A4kinen" title="Tommi Mäkinen">Tommi Mäkinen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shekhar_Mehta" title="Shekhar Mehta">Shekhar Mehta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Sainz" title="Carlos Sainz">Carlos Sainz</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Colin_McRae" title="Colin McRae">Colin McRae</a>. Although the rally still runs annually as part of the Africa rally championship, the organisers are hoping to be allowed to rejoin the World Rally championship in the next couple of years. </p>
      <p>Nairobi has hosted several major continental sports events, including the <a href="/wiki/FIBA_Africa_Championship_1993" title="FIBA Africa Championship 1993">FIBA Africa Championship 1993</a>, where <a href="/wiki/Kenya_national_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Kenya national basketball team">Kenya's national basketball team</a> finished in the top four, its best performance to date.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ugali_%26_Sukuma_Wiki.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Ugali_%26_Sukuma_Wiki.jpg/220px-Ugali_%26_Sukuma_Wiki.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Ugali_%26_Sukuma_Wiki.jpg/330px-Ugali_%26_Sukuma_Wiki.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Ugali_%26_Sukuma_Wiki.jpg/440px-Ugali_%26_Sukuma_Wiki.jpg 2x" data-file-width="576" data-file-height="380"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ugali_%26_Sukuma_Wiki.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Ugali" title="Ugali">Ugali</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sukuma_wiki" title="Sukuma wiki">sukuma wiki</a>, staples of Kenyan cuisine
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Kenyans generally have three meals in a day—breakfast (<i>kiamsha kinywa</i>), lunch (<i>chakula cha mchana</i>), and supper (<i>chakula cha jioni</i> or simply <i>chajio</i>). In between, they have the 10-o'clock tea (<i>chai ya saa nne</i>) and 4&nbsp;p.m. tea (<i>chai ya saa kumi</i>). Breakfast is usually tea or porridge with bread, <a href="/wiki/Chapati" title="Chapati">chapati</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mahamri" class="mw-redirect" title="Mahamri">mahamri</a>, boiled sweet potatoes, or <a href="/wiki/Yam_(vegetable)" title="Yam (vegetable)">yams</a>. <a href="/wiki/Githeri" title="Githeri">Githeri</a> is a common lunchtime dish in many households, while <a href="/wiki/Ugali" title="Ugali">Ugali</a> with vegetables, sour milk (<a href="/wiki/Mursik" title="Mursik">mursik</a>), meat, fish, or any other stew is generally eaten by much of the population for lunch or supper. Regional variations and dishes also exist. </p>
      <p>In western Kenya, among the <a href="/wiki/Luo_(Kenya_and_Tanzania)" class="mw-redirect" title="Luo (Kenya and Tanzania)">Luo</a>, fish is a common dish; among the <a href="/wiki/Kalenjin_people" title="Kalenjin people">Kalenjin</a>, who dominate much of the Rift Valley Region, mursik—sour milk—is a common drink. </p>
      <p>In cities such as <a href="/wiki/Nairobi" title="Nairobi">Nairobi</a>, there are fast-food restaurants, including <a href="/wiki/Steers" title="Steers">Steers</a>, <a href="/wiki/KFC" title="KFC">KFC</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Subway_(restaurant)" title="Subway (restaurant)">Subway</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup> There are also many fish-and-chips shops.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Cheese_in_Kenya" title="Cheese in Kenya">Cheese</a> is becoming more popular in Kenya, with consumption increasing particularly among the middle class.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup> </p>

                <th scope="col" class="navbox-title" colspan="2" style="background:#e8e8ff;">
                 <div id="25px_Geographic_locale" style="font-size:114%;margin:0 4em">
                  <a href="/wiki/File:Gnome-globe.svg" class="image"><img alt="Gnome-globe.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Gnome-globe.svg/25px-Gnome-globe.svg.png" decoding="async" width="25" height="25" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Gnome-globe.svg/38px-Gnome-globe.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Gnome-globe.svg/50px-Gnome-globe.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="48" data-file-height="48"></a><span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>Geographic locale

               <tr>

                 <div style="padding:0px"> <b><a href="/wiki/Geographic_coordinate_system" title="Geographic coordinate system">Lat. <small>and</small> Long.</a>
